  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a4b43215-77e8-4d46-ae1c-68f8d5c7607e'
      });

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer1056170454553936810">Sometimes it is the one who loves you who hurts you the most.<br/><br/>Lily hasn’t always had it easy, but that’s never stopped her from working hard for the life she wants. She’s come a long way from the small town in Maine where she grew up<br/> — she graduated from college, moved to Boston, and started her own business. So when she feels a spark with a gorgeous neurosurgeon named Ryle</span>
  <span id="freeText1056170454553936810" style="display:none">Sometimes it is the one who loves you who hurts you the most.<br /><br />Lily hasn’t always had it easy, but that’s never stopped her from working hard for the life she wants. She’s come a long way from the small town in Maine where she grew up<br /> — she graduated from college, moved to Boston, and started her own business. So when she feels a spark with a gorgeous neurosurgeon named Ryle Kincaid, everything in Lily’s life suddenly seems almost too good to be true.<br /><br />Ryle is assertive, stubborn, maybe even a little arrogant. He’s also sensitive, brilliant, and has a total soft spot for Lily. And the way he looks in scrubs certainly doesn’t hurt. Lily can’t get him out of her head. But Ryle’s complete aversion to relationships is disturbing. Even as Lily finds herself becoming the exception to his “no dating” rule, she can’t help but wonder what made him that way in the first place.<br /><br />As questions about her new relationship overwhelm her, so do thoughts of Atlas Corrigan — her first love and a link to the past she left behind. He was her kindred spirit, her protector. When Atlas suddenly reappears, everything Lily has built with Ryle is threatened.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1056170454553936810" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div id="review_1166436547" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1166436547" />
    <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog"><img alt="Aestas Book Blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353371225p2/5604583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1166436547?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aestas Book Blog" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog">Aestas Book Blog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5604583-aestas-book-blog?shelf=not-yet-released">not-yet-released</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5604583-aestas-book-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1166436547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17804351989982592404"><b> ::: SPOILER-FREE REVIEW ::: </b><br/><img width='100%' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466643696i/19502975.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <strong>
    <em>Fifteen seconds. That’s all it takes to completely change everything about a person. Fifteen seconds that we’ll never get back.</em>
  </strong>
</blockquote><br/>HOLY WOW! <em>It Ends With Us</em> is one of the most <strong>powerful</strong> books of 2016 and one of the most raw, honest, inspiring, and profoundly beautiful stories I've ever read. It wasn’t anything like what I expected, but it delivered so much more than I ever hoped for. This is the kind of book that I want to give to every woman and just be like…</span>
  <span id="freeText17804351989982592404" style="display:none"><b> ::: SPOILER-FREE REVIEW ::: </b><br><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466643696i/19502975.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <strong>
    <em>Fifteen seconds. That’s all it takes to completely change everything about a person. Fifteen seconds that we’ll never get back.</em>
  </strong>
</blockquote><br>HOLY WOW! <em>It Ends With Us</em> is one of the most <strong>powerful</strong> books of 2016 and one of the most raw, honest, inspiring, and profoundly beautiful stories I've ever read. It wasn’t anything like what I expected, but it delivered so much more than I ever hoped for. This is the kind of book that I want to give to every woman and just be like… READ THIS BOOK. NOW. Come to think of it, all the men should read it too. EVERYONE should read this book. Absolutely everyone. It's a story of unshakable love and finding the strength to make the right choice in the hardest situation. I honestly don't think I've ever been prouder of a heroine. I've loved Colleen Hoover's books for a long time because she always writes unique stories... and this one left a lasting mark on my heart. It is a MUST-READ!!<br><br>This is a completely 
  <strong>spoiler-free review</strong>
. I'm not even going to add the blurb or tell you what this book is about. It's a Colleen Hoover book. That should be enough to tell you it's amazing. But I really feel that you should just dive into this book without knowing anything about the plot. To be honest, I'm the usually the kind of reader who likes to know every little thing about what to expect in advance, but I've really learned to trust Colleen's writing and her storytelling so even I went into this book without knowing anything at all... and I was blown away by the story!<br><br>This book is <em>unputdownable</em>. You'll notice as you read that there are no good stopping points. None at all. I began reading it late at night and every time I tried to put it down to go to sleep, I just had to get back up and keep reading because I couldn't stop thinking about it. I didn't finish until almost 5AM but my gosh was it ever worth it!<br><br>Of all the heroines I've ever read, Lily was most certainly one of the ones I admired the most. I knew loved her from the first few pages, but having finished the book, I truly couldn't be prouder of her. Her strength and conviction over the course of this story made her into a heroine I'd want every girl and woman to read about and look up to. She was so real and vulnerable as we all are, but the strength with which she took control of her life was admirable on such a deep level. I just wanted to hug her and cheer. I don't think I've been this proud of a fictional character before.<br><br>There's an incredibly <em>powerful message</em> in this book that is very subtly woven in from the start. It begins in the first chapter, but you don't yet realize how <em>significant</em> each of these moments truly are... and as you read more, these pieces of the story come together forming a scenario that gives such a raw, honest portrayal of an incredibly relevant issue. I'm not mentioning it on purpose because I don't want you to expect it. <em>The fact that it's unexpected for you as the reader is very important because it's also unexpected for the heroine.</em> As she begins to realize what kind of situation she's in, so do you. And this realization very much allows you to experience her journey <em>with</em> her.<br><br>The only thing I want to address head on is the question of the 'love triangle' because a few of you have read the blurb and have asked about it. All I want to say is to please try and move away from that thought. I don't want to spoil the plot at all, but that is so not what this book is about. That is not the point, or the focus. Whatever it is you're thinking this book is, just trust me -- it's so much bigger than that. Seriously, trust Colleen. I did.<br><br>As a romance reader, I found this book incredibly refreshing. As much as I adore the romance genre (and I really do), it sometimes can get a little repetative. As both an avid reader and a blogger, I'm always looking for books that step outside the lines a little; ones that do something different or take the issues a little deeper. This book represented exactly what I wish I could be reading all the time -- not this literal story, but just the fact that it went in such a different direction and gave me such an unexpected story that left me with such a strong message.<br><br>One of the things that intrigued me the most and had me wondering when I heard about this book was what the title really meant -- and there's this very specific moment when the title is echoed in the story that just had such a <strong>strong</strong> impact as I read it. That was my cheer moment. I just sat back and went 'woah!'. The title is truly perfect.<br><br>In order to write this review, I went back over the book a second time and one thing I noticed strongly was how many intricate layers there were to the story that I couldn't possibly have known about in my first read. I loved that this is one of those books you experience differently (in a good way) both the first and second time though.<br><br>I have to say that this book would make a <em>seriously amazing movie</em>. I could picture every scene so clearly as I read. This is also such an incredibly relevant story for many people -- whether they've personally been through what happened to Lily or they know of someone who has -- so I really do hope that one day this makes it to the big screen.<br><br>My copy of this book is literally filled with highlighted quotes in every single chapter but I made a conscious decision not to add any to this review because I really truly do not want to give anything away about the story. Just trust me and jump into this story blind. I promise that it is a reading experience you don't want to miss.<br><br>This began as one of my most highly anticipated books of 2016 and it is now of my top favorite books of the year. I was unable to put it down from the moment I started reading and I know that this is one of those profoundly beautiful and unforgettable stories that will stay with me for a long time. I highly recommend it to <em>
  <strong>everyone</strong>
</em>!<br><blockquote>
  <strong>
    <em>That’s what fifteen minutes can do to a person. It can destroy them.<br>It can save them.</em>
  </strong>
</blockquote><br><strong>Rating: 5+ STARS! Standalone.</strong><br> <br> 	 <strong><a href="http://amzn.to/1pAn5Ki" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Pre-order IT ENDS WITH US (Kindle)</a></strong> <br> 	 <strong><a href="http://amzn.to/1MUSiDh" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Pre-order IT ENDS WITH US (Paperback)</a></strong> <br> <br>Note: If you <a href="http://amzn.to/1pAn5Ki" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">pre-order a copy</a>, it'll automatically be delivered to your Kindle on release day so that you don't forget!<br><br>__________________________<br><br><b> For more of my reviews, book news and updates:<br>✦ <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Main blog: Aestas Book Blog</a><br>✦ <a href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/Aestas-Book-Blog/332404836826905" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook Blog Page</a><br>✦ <a href="https://twitter.com/AestasBookBlog" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> <br>✦ <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com/subscribe/" rel="nofollow noopener">Subscribe by email</a> <br><br><a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener"><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380306821i/688100._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> </b></span>

<div id="review_1164705482" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1164705482" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1164705482?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1164705482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11598408337357888418"><b>5 + brave and bold stars!!!</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%209/A4805447-C439-4036-88A6-0D169567BB66_zps8cqal3cy.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469710749i/19848841._SY540_.jpg' alt=' photo A4805447-C439-4036-88A6-0D169567BB66_zps8cqal3cy.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Want the naked truth about <i>It Ends with Us</i>? Reading this book will change your life. It’s so different from any of Colleen Hoover’s other books. You can tell it’s heavier, more personal, just more. This book is deep. It’s profound. It’s a book that needs to be read. I'll repeat: <b>THIS IS A BOOK THAT NEEDS TO BE READ!</b> <br/><br/>This story is moving. It will make you think about things that are uncomfortable to think about. It will lift your heart, devastate you at times, make </span>
  <span id="freeText11598408337357888418" style="display:none"><b>5 + brave and bold stars!!!</b><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%209/A4805447-C439-4036-88A6-0D169567BB66_zps8cqal3cy.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469710749i/19848841._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo A4805447-C439-4036-88A6-0D169567BB66_zps8cqal3cy.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Want the naked truth about <i>It Ends with Us</i>? Reading this book will change your life. It’s so different from any of Colleen Hoover’s other books. You can tell it’s heavier, more personal, just more. This book is deep. It’s profound. It’s a book that needs to be read. I'll repeat: <b>THIS IS A BOOK THAT NEEDS TO BE READ!</b> <br><br>This story is moving. It will make you think about things that are uncomfortable to think about. It will lift your heart, devastate you at times, make you proud, fill you with sorrow and make you smile. It will move you. It’s powerful and intense in the best way, but also has hopeful and lighter moments. The story itself is one that has been heavy on my heart from the moment I finished it. <br><br>Sometimes, I read a book and it’s so beautiful, influential and emotional I will cry just thinking about the characters and their story. Not in a bad way necessarily, I just get that moved and that emotional while thinking about it. That is this book. Trying to find the words for this review is bringing me to tears. It’s hard to explain the story completely spoiler free, but this isn’t a ‘sad’ book. It’s a strength book. Because dealing with the issues in this story took so much strength. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%209/A921F34A-F1FD-40F6-9F3F-4D56EEEEC792_zpsnozh6abt.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469710749i/19848842._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo A921F34A-F1FD-40F6-9F3F-4D56EEEEC792_zpsnozh6abt.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I’m not going to talk about the actual story at all, but I will speak a bit about the characters. <b>Lily</b>. Speaking of strength, Lily may be the strongest heroine that I’ve read about. Your strength is really tested when you are put in a hard situation where your choices are impossible. I loved Lily so much. I was proud of Lily and the choices she made. I want to be Lily when I grow up. <br><i>
  <blockquote>Fifteen seconds. That’s all it takes to completely change everything about a person. Fifteen seconds that we’ll never get back.</blockquote>
</i><br>There are two men in this story, but please don’t think this is a triangle book. It’s not. It’s hard to explain, but it’s not. <b>Ryle</b> is a charming guy. He’s a giving person. He’s got a lot of great attributes. I’m not sure if I’ve ever felt so conflicted over a character as I did him. <b>Atlas</b> is the type of man I always have a soft spot for as a reader. His story gutted me at times, but he is also a character with a lot of strength and so much beauty. I loved Atlas from the second I met him and that love never stopped throughout the book. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%209/685F34F5-4C70-4859-B7FB-28151B38FB18_zps1r58ysog.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469710749i/19848843._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 685F34F5-4C70-4859-B7FB-28151B38FB18_zps1r58ysog.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>
  <blockquote>“Lily?” he whispers, looking at me sincerely. “You just might be the best thing that’s ever happened to me.”</blockquote>
</i> Aside from the three main characters in the story, Lily’s mom played a prominent part. Their relationship played an even bigger part. Ryle’s sister and Lily’s best friend Alyssa was one of my favorite characters in this book. When things got hard she was there. One line she said in the book, to Lily just solidified the type of woman she was. Coleen always writes that one side character that you love so hard in her stories, and Alyssa was that character for me. I can’t not mention Ellen, because, well, it’s Ellen. That part was brilliant. It made me smile every time Ellen was mentioned. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%209/4842FA37-D99B-4299-A257-69C0022519B4_zpsio43lvpp.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469710749i/19848844._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 4842FA37-D99B-4299-A257-69C0022519B4_zpsio43lvpp.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>When reading this book, there were moments I struggled between not being able to tear my eyes away from the page, and others I had to take a breather because I couldn't handle what was going on.Parts of this story left me so heartbroken and others lifted me up so high. There are some parts that are just so powerful I could only read them in awe. This is it. This is why I read. Books like this. <br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>All humans make mistakes. What determines a person’s character aren’t the mistakes we make. It’s how we take those mistakes and turn them into lessons rather than excuses.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b> Colleen Hoover is an author who truly has a way with words. She killed this book. I’ve read and loved all of CoHo’s books. Some of her earlier books are some of my all-time favorites. I’ve enjoyed all of her latest books, but this is by far the best book she’s ever written. And it’s tied with <i>Hopeless</i> as my own personal favorite book by her. And that is saying a lot, because <i>Hopeless</i> is one of my top books ever.   <br><br>If you only read one book this year, let it be <i>It Ends with Us</i>. Everyone needs to read this book. 5+ star favorite. Completely unforgettable and highly recommended! <br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“It stops here. With me and you. It ends with us.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i> <br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%209/1410EA85-DC54-43C8-8DE1-722CEEE3D402_zpsnihnrbzy.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469710749i/19848845._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 1410EA85-DC54-43C8-8DE1-722CEEE3D402_zpsnihnrbzy.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<div id="review_1715766737" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1715766737" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1715766737?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1715766737" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17198920650718242793"><blockquote>
  <i>Preventing your heart from forgiving someone you love is actually a hell of a lot harder than simply forgiving them.</i>
</blockquote><br/>4 1/2 stars. <b>Holy crap, what a book.</b> This is unlike anything Hoover has written before. I have so many emotions right now that it's hard to know where to start, but I think everyone should read this book. That's right: everyone. <br/><br/>I could easily give everything away. I could, but I won't. If you go looking for lots of reviews, it won't be hard to work out what <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27362503.It_Ends_with_Us' title='It Ends with Us by Colleen Hoover' rel='nofollow noopener'>It Ends with Us</a> is </span>
  <span id="freeText17198920650718242793" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Preventing your heart from forgiving someone you love is actually a hell of a lot harder than simply forgiving them.</i>
</blockquote><br />4 1/2 stars. <b>Holy crap, what a book.</b> This is unlike anything Hoover has written before. I have so many emotions right now that it's hard to know where to start, but I think everyone should read this book. That's right: everyone. <br /><br />I could easily give everything away. I could, but I won't. If you go looking for lots of reviews, it won't be hard to work out what <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27362503.It_Ends_with_Us" title="It Ends with Us by Colleen Hoover" rel="nofollow noopener">It Ends with Us</a> is about. And if you do, you should still read it, but I think it's better if you don't. I think you should go into this book knowing as little as possible. Just realize that this is something very different from Hoover's usual new adult romances (that I admittedly have had <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/691155108" rel="nofollow noopener">all</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793673782" rel="nofollow noopener">kinds</a> of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1438941130" rel="nofollow noopener">problems</a> with).<br /><br />So I don't want to say too much, but this is an <b>extremely powerful story</b> and it's not what most people will be expecting. It gets its power from the singular first person narrative (I'm honestly not a big fan of the alternating male/female POV romances) and we experience everything through Lily's eyes. When she falls in love, we fall in love; when her heart is broken, our heart is broken; when she gets it all wrong, so do we.<br /><br />I cannot stress how important and <i>damn smart</i> this book is. There is no black and white characterization - it's much deeper and more complex than that, and therefore, far more emotional. <br /><br />It peels back the layers of characters and relationships to do something that so many other authors have tried and failed to do - to make you understand a situation that for most people makes no sense. It's <b>very sad, painful and exceptionally honest</b>. My heart hurt while reading it and I almost cried several times.<br /><br />As well as all this emotion and sadness that I'm being coy about, Hoover also brings out some of her very best writing. Little gems of honesty about human nature and relationships that are all the more painful because of their resounding truth. It's such a quotable book, but unfortunately most of the quotes are spoilers, so I shall refrain from posting them.<br /><br />There's so many great things to mention, but I keep getting distracted by my <b>feelings</b>. The narrative is interspersed with letters that Lily wrote as a teenager and they are addressed to Ellen Degeneres - a strange touch that ends up being absolutely perfect. Shit, just writing this review and remembering the story is an emotional experience.<br /><br />And then there's the <b>absolutely fantastic female friendship</b>. I want Allysa to be my best friend. Hoover clearly knows her audience of 16-25 year old women, creating characters with their quirks and habits - Allysa, for example, is a self-confessed "Pinterest whore", which made me laugh. But seriously, she is the best friend ever and she says one of the most perfect lines in this book.<br /><br />Anyway, I'm just going to start rambling soon because I read this book in a whirlwind of emotions throughout a single day. I've been up since a ridiculous time and I need to go sleep now. But really, give this book a chance. I thought it was excellent.<br /><br />Trigger Warnings: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Domestic abuse (physical, occasionally graphic). Attempted rape. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /> <a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17198920650718242793" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1496762730" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1496762730" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30035966-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523817330p2/30035966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1496762730?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/30035966-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=5-star-favorites">5-star-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=read-it-and-weep">read-it-and-weep</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1496762730" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13107912307185581147"><i>It Ends With Us</i>... Wow I really don't know what to truly say about this novel. This review will be a little light because, like most CoHo books, you'll want to go into it with little to no information. I went into this book thinking it was going to be this one thing, and it turned out to be the complete opposite. <br/><br/><i>IEWU </i>follows Lily, a girl in her early twenties, who has never had it easy. Though coming from a family that was better off she has always had to work for the things she's wanted. After</span>
  <span id="freeText13107912307185581147" style="display:none"><i>It Ends With Us</i>... Wow I really don't know what to truly say about this novel. This review will be a little light because, like most CoHo books, you'll want to go into it with little to no information. I went into this book thinking it was going to be this one thing, and it turned out to be the complete opposite. <br><br><i>IEWU </i>follows Lily, a girl in her early twenties, who has never had it easy. Though coming from a family that was better off she has always had to work for the things she's wanted. After graduating college she gets up and moves to Boston and hopes to start her own business. While there she meets and falls for Ryle, a thriving neurosurgeon who is determined to be the best in his field. The two hit it off hard, and things seem almost too good to be true. Ryle is everything that Lily is not. He is forward, assertive, and stubborn. He is also a lot of thing Lily is; he is strong, passionate, and motivated. Though the two have an immediate connections and sparks fly, the two decided to take their time getting to know one another. Lily is such a beautifully written leading lady. I loved getting to grow with her and be apart of her journey. I loved hearing her thoughts and seeing how she processed things. When I was first reading and got to the point where she does her journal entries, but she does them so they are letters to Ellen DeGeneres, I thought I wasn't going to like that aspect of it. The first few had me thinking "<i>this is a little cheesy</i>", but the more I got into it the more I started to enjoy them. They really tied Lily's past and present perfectly together. As Lily's and Ryle's relationship pushes forward she finds herself looking back at those entries and thoughts of her first love Atlas resurface. Atlas was her first everything and was the biggest impact on her life. Atlas was the homeless boy who found his way into the abandoned house next door. Atlas and Lily as teens formed an unlikely friendship. Sharing everything and having a bond that no one around them seemed to understand. Spending every possible moment together and having so many stolen ones the two were kindred spirits. When Atlas reappears in the story it truly threatens everything Lily and Ryle have. (not a spoiler it's given he eventually will). Both Ryle and Atlas bring such important and different aspects to this story. I think CoHo manages to make them both such polar opposites, but at the same time manages to make them mesh so well.The characters in the book, main or side, all feel so realistic and authentic. <br><br>When it comes to the plot there is almost nothing I can say about it. I hope everyone will do the same to keep things from getting spoiled. The story is an emotional roller coaster from start to finish. It's one of those books that you will have a thousand theories about and all of them will be wrong. I kept trying to guess what I thought might happen next and in classic Hoover style she managed to surprise me. This book was solid from page one and was steady throughout, but around the 80% mark is where things really took a turn (in the best way possible).  <i>IEWU </i>hit me on such a personal level. I didn't expect this book to impact me so hard. It had everything I wanted from a New Adult read. It's very classic CoHo, but it also branches out somewhere she's never been before, but she does it with such ease. She manages to weave these heavy moments with ones that will make you swoon, laugh, and then cry. My favorite part of this book though, was the author's note. Usually author's notes are at the beginning of the story, however it is so important that this one was left for the end. It took a book that was good and made it exceptional! God, this note effected me like so few books have. It made me cry fifty times harder than the entire book or anything Colleen's ever written.<br><br><a href="https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-MpIUTbusCqE/V4Lt7xXnzuI/AAAAAAAADpo/RQ7dkfLGPbop_lDteWmZ4LoXnBmHd43PACLcB/s1600/iewu1.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="175" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469745413ra/19853525.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Finding out how important this book was for her to write will hit you hard, but I hope she also knows how important it is as a reader to read. Knowing where an author gets their ideas from can change your whole outlook on a book, and this one... this one broke me.</b><br><br><b>Thank you Colleen Hoover for continuing to gift the reading community with your words.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13107912307185581147" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1722972018" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1722972018" />
    <a title="K.L. Grayson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30778025-k-l-grayson"><img alt="K.L. Grayson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406510220p2/30778025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1722972018?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K.L. Grayson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K.L. Grayson" href="/user/show/30778025-k-l-grayson">K.L. Grayson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1722972018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10320245797990411718">Dear Colleen,<br/><br/>I find it fitting that I write this review as a letter to you the way Lily would write to Ellen. Don't ask me why, I really don't know. What I do know is that I haven't been on Goodreads in nearly six months and it's entirely your fault that i'm here now. So, if i stumble upon a poor review on one of my books and end up in the fetal position on my kitchen floor surrounded by Ding Dong wrappers, well, I'm blaming it on you. I've even given my husband instructions to bill you for the </span>
  <span id="freeText10320245797990411718" style="display:none">Dear Colleen,<br /><br />I find it fitting that I write this review as a letter to you the way Lily would write to Ellen. Don't ask me why, I really don't know. What I do know is that I haven't been on Goodreads in nearly six months and it's entirely your fault that i'm here now. So, if i stumble upon a poor review on one of my books and end up in the fetal position on my kitchen floor surrounded by Ding Dong wrappers, well, I'm blaming it on you. I've even given my husband instructions to bill you for the psychiatry bill if that happens.<br /><br />On Friday I had a hysterectomy. It wasn't the worst day of my life, but it certainly wasn't the best. One chapter of my life--quite possibly the best chapter--ended. The surgery itself took twenty minutes. Twenty minutes. Can you believe that? Twenty minutes to take out the uterus that carried my three beautiful babies for a total of twenty eight months. Twenty minutes to change my life. Don't feel bad for me, that's not what I want. The offending organ had to come out, I knew this. But it didn't make it any easier. It didn't make the finality of the situation any easier. In all honesty, for a couple of minutes I didn't just feel like a chapter was ending, more like an entire flipping book. Maybe my life isn't made up of chapters, maybe it's part of a duet, or a trilogy? Either way, part of my story was over. <br /><br />Over a matter of several hours, I slowly woke up from surgery and at one point I remember sitting there and just staring at the wall paper in my hospital room. <br /><br />My uterus was gone. <br /><br />Mauve diamonds. <br /><br />The wallpaper was covered in mauve diamonds.<br /><br />That's the most hideous color, don't you think? Mauve. Not quite pink. Not quite maroon. <br /><br />I counted seven hundred and fifty three diamonds before I allowed the first tear to fall. But I wasn't just crying for losing a part of my body, and I wasn't crying for losing the ability to carry more children. I was crying because some women don't even get to experience what I've gotten to experience. Some women never get to have babies. They never get to feel them grow in their bellies. They never get to see the slimy little monsters as they tumble their way into this world.<br /><br />And I did.<br /><br />I got to do all of that three times.<br /><br />So why was I so upset? What the hell was my problem? I should be grateful, right? Happy?<br /><br />My husband slept soundly in the chair, snoring softly, but at some point my cries must have woken him up. He stirred and I did the only thing I could do ... I grabbed your book. You see, it was sitting on my bedside table. I buried my nose between the pages and when my better half asked me if I was okay I simply peeked over the top of the book and whispered, "Colleen. She did it again."<br /><br />I didn't need to say much more, he knows my obsession with your words and I found myself grateful. Grateful that he knew your books make me cry and grateful that you inadvertently allowed me to grieve. And that's what I did. I read your book and I grieved. I cried when Lily cried. I cried when Ryle cried. And even when no one was crying, I still cried simply because I needed to and I could and no one thought twice about it because i was reading and that's what i do when i read. It was my outlet, my excuse for the tears that wouldn't go away, the tears that kept falling despite my desperate protest.<br /><br />I cried for all of the Lily's in the world, and the Ryle's too. I cried for the Atlas'. And I cried for the Kirby's (that's my name. No i'm not named after a vacuum, or a cream puff)<br /><br />But you see, I didn't want to cry. I didn't want to be upset. I have three beautiful children whom I love with my entire heart. My body did it's job extremely well and that is something to be proud of. But why wasn't I proud? <br /><br />Naked truth?<br /><br />I'm selfish.<br />I wanted one more baby even though my husband didn't. I wanted one more baby when there are women out there that can't have any at all.<br /><br />So why am I telling you this? My story is nothing like Lily's. Not even close. <br />But maybe it is ... <br />She wanted something she shouldn't want. I wanted something I couldn't have. She had a decision to make ... one that would change her life. So did I. She made a decision that was right for her and for her life at that particular time. <br />Ditto.<br />But the real reason I'm telling you this is because for two days I was drowning and It Ends With Us was my lifeline. It's what I grabbed when I needed to stop thinking ... it's what I grabbed when i needed to cry ... and when i finally finished the book and put it down, it wasn't mauve diamonds that I saw ... it was my smiling children.<br /><br />My three beautiful smiling children ... and my niece Lily. <br /><br />-- Kirby</span>
  <a data-text-id="10320245797990411718" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1712522490?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/16384209-candace">Candace</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/31355608-it-ends-with-us">review of another edition</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=pregnant-heroines">pregnant-heroines</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1712522490" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16391648761808472606">Phenomenal! <br/><br/>This book will make you fall in love, rip your heart out and force you to reconsider your preconceived ideas about abuse. This is the most moving book that I've read in a LONG time. It was absolutely addicting, but so difficult at times. I don't cry very often, but this one had me crying big, fat tears. <br/><br/>It's been a couple of days since I finished 'It Ends With Us' and I'm still thinking about Lily's story. It's one that'll hang with you. In so many ways, her story gutted me. Yet, it </span>
  <span id="freeText16391648761808472606" style="display:none">Phenomenal! <br /><br />This book will make you fall in love, rip your heart out and force you to reconsider your preconceived ideas about abuse. This is the most moving book that I've read in a LONG time. It was absolutely addicting, but so difficult at times. I don't cry very often, but this one had me crying big, fat tears. <br /><br />It's been a couple of days since I finished 'It Ends With Us' and I'm still thinking about Lily's story. It's one that'll hang with you. In so many ways, her story gutted me. Yet, it was also inspiring.<br /><br />Lily grows up in an abusive household. After watching her mother suffer for years at the hand of her father, she tells herself that she'll never allow any man to treat her that way. She grows into a strong and independent woman, leaving behind the horrors of her childhood...Or so she thinks.<br /><br />Despite everything she's promised herself, Lily finds herself in an abusive relationship. The behavior and cycle is so insidious that you almost can't believe what is happening. Ms. Hoover manages to weave the violence into a relationship that is otherwise seemingly perfect. It is so skillfully written that you won't want to believe what you've read. <br /><br /> I found myself making excuses for the abuser. I didn't want to believe that he wouldn't change. For the first time, I could understand why women make excuses for abusers. I can only imagine how strong that pull must be in reality if I felt so strongly about a fictional character. <br /><br />I am in awe of Lily. Her strength and conviction blew me away. I don't think I would've been strong enough to do what she did. She was an amazing character.<br /><br />This was a beautiful and heartbreaking book. I recommend it to everyone. It is a must read.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16391648761808472606" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar">Kelly (and the Book Boar)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=everyone-loved-it-but-me">everyone-loved-it-but-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=crunken-love">crunken-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=the-great-white-hype">the-great-white-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=hot-mess-express">hot-mess-express</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=denied-the-arc">denied-the-arc</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1729054812" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4816818238891132320">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/>“What a great time to have a dissenting opinion about a book written by an author with a particularly rabid fanbase!” said no one ever. In case we haven’t met and you’re seeing this review due to the new <b>IN YO’ FACE!</b> Goodreads format which shares reviews/updates to your feed errrrrrrrry single time one of your friends likes or comments on them, allow me to introduce myself. My name is Kelly . . . . <br/><br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471365238i/20037588.jpg' alt='commercial photography locations' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Also, I spoil things, so back awa</span>
  <span id="freeText4816818238891132320" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br>“What a great time to have a dissenting opinion about a book written by an author with a particularly rabid fanbase!” said no one ever. In case we haven’t met and you’re seeing this review due to the new <b>IN YO’ FACE!</b> Goodreads format which shares reviews/updates to your feed errrrrrrrry single time one of your friends likes or comments on them, allow me to introduce myself. My name is Kelly . . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471365238i/20037588.jpg" alt="commercial photography locations" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Also, I spoil things, so back away quickly if you don’t want this one to be ruined for you.<br><br>My glaring 1 Star in a sea of 5s probably makes it pretty clear that I detested this book, but please refrain from fetching your torches and pitchforks for a moment and take note that not only did I <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1715924395?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">just 5 Star a CoHo Story two weeks ago</a> (as well as shoved it down everyone’s throats I possibly could), but also I want to make all of the sexuals with Miles Archer and will fight anyone for dibs on his imaginary lurv making. I didn’t pick this up in order to hate on it. I’m one of you . . . . sometimes. Definitely not this time, but lots of times. And this is why I don’t ever give up on Hoover novels. I never know how I’m going to react.<br><br>Allow me to explain what went wrong for me with this one . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471365238ra/20037589.gif" alt="commercial photography locations" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Let’s start with the obvious annoyances that seem to be in nearly every NA book that drive me batshit before getting to the real nitty gritty. First, the character names. Ryle, Lily Bloom and Atlas???????<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471365238ra/20037590.gif" alt="commercial photography locations" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Is it against the law to <b>not</b> use absolutely ridiculous (™Ron2.0) names in these books???? <br><br>Second . . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>“Your lips. I love how they’re as red as your hair.”</i>
</b><br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471365238ra/20037591.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>According to Google (all hail Google) less than 2% of the world’s population has red hair, and yet 99.998% of all NA leading ladies do. Just stahp.<br><br>Third, non-existent chemistry. In this story Lily and Ryle meet by chance on a rooftop after experiencing respective miserable days. In a matter of minutes Lily goes from worrying the stranger on the roof could be a psycho killer/rapist to getting into his super sexy (NOT) pick-up lines . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>“If you wouldn’t sleep with someone you just met . . .” His eyes meet mine again. “Exactly how far would you go?”</i>
</b><br><br>Ewww. She already said thanks but no thanks freakshow so STFU.<br><br>Now let’s move on to the real big issue. I took a gander at my friends’ reviews before I started typing this and noticed my buddy <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1722358128?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Chelsea</a> was the only other naysayer in the batch. She summed it up <b>perfectly</b> when she talked about the massive amounts of emotional manipulation that was forced down the readers’ throats in order to make them feel all the things.<br><br>It’s a running joke with my friends/family/co-workers that I have a robot heart. And for the majority of the time it’s true. I generally experience two emotions – happiness and annoyance. But even a robot like me can be manipulated into having a feeling/crying the ugly tears like a Kardashian once in a blue moon (*cough <i>Me Before You</i> cough*). This time, though? It was like a flashing neon sign . . . . <br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471365238ra/20037592.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>To begin with, our first leading male Atlas is a homeless teenager who Lily befriends/eventually loses her virginity. In case you don’t get the writing on the wall, Atlas is being set up as the most perfect perfection that ever perfected. He’s also the way to getting the “raised in an abusive household” plotline uncovered. Like in all NA stories, Atlas and Lily are torn apart. Lily moves on with her life, graduates college, yada yada, and, as mentioned above, meet-cutes <s>super creeper</s> Mr. Right 2.0 on the roof. Mr. Right 2.0 is not only another most perfect perfection that ever perfected, but he’s also <b>rich</b> and a <b>neurosurgeon</b> and very obviously husband material even though he’s never had a girlfriend (also after dating only six months), <b>annnnnnnnd</b> due to their mutually busy schedules not really knowing the guy.<br><br>It wasn’t too hard to see where the story was going to go (and no, I hadn’t been spoiled because I didn’t read any reviews or the synopsis, I just auto-request everything by Hoover from both NetGalley and the library). Basically this was a story about domestic abuse and making excuses not only the first time he knocks your ass down “on accident” but also the second time when you wake up after “falling” down the stairs and hearing his sob story about a superbadawful that effed him up as a kid and then agreeing on a policy where <b>
  <i>“When you’re upset, just walk away. And I’ll walk away”</i>
</b> (because <b>THAT’S</b> going to fucking work) and then saying <b>
  <i>“It’s okay, Ryle. It’s okay. You were angry, it’s okay”</i>
</b> and making sure even when you’re bleeding profusely out of your fucking skull and are concussed and have quite possibly just been raped by your own damn husband that you get taken to an emergency room in a hospital other than the one where your bastard abuser works in order to protect his ass as well as explaining <b>
  <i> “sometimes the reason women go back is simply because they’re in love”</i>
</b> and in case all that wasn’t e-fucking-nough you add in a whoopsie baby (another NA per usual) to serve as the wake-up call that maybe it’d be a good idea to ditch this zero and eventually find you a hero, <b>buuuuuuuuuuuut</b> you just come to an agreement regarding visitation and whathaveyou rather than involving the court and much needed supervised interaction because you <b>know</b> he wouldn’t hurt the baby since it’s obvious he loves her . . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471365238i/20037593._SY540_.jpg" alt="commercial photography locations" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Nope. <br><br>I’m well aware I’m going against the grain here. I give zero fucks. Don’t bother trolling me to tell me how stupid I am (especially if you’re a teenager who has lived a privileged lifestyle and never experienced anything contained in this book for yourself). I went to the wholesale club yesterday and stocked up on big ol’ batch of . . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471365238i/20037594._SY540_.jpg" alt="commercial photography locations" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I will be using it freely.<br><br><i>Many thanks to the library for having nearly <b>every</b> book I ever want to read – especially books like these that are only approved to fangirling 5 Star reviewers prior to publication.</i><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="4816818238891132320" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1613197349" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1613197349" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1613197349?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=abuse">abuse</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer17956450184343634184">*Spoilers*<br/><br/>I did not see that coming.<br/><br/>Which I think is the whole point. <br/><br/>Ever since I was fifteen, I promised myself I would never get into a relationship with someone before I knew what they looked like angry. Are they the type to grow exasperated and leave the room, shout their lungs out or… aggressively hit their loved ones?<br/><br/>I’m very happy with the way Colleen Hoover dealt with the subject of abuse. It’s very well explored and the connection between Lily and her mother so beautiful yet so sad. Bu</span>
  <span id="freeText17956450184343634184" style="display:none">*Spoilers*<br /><br />I did not see that coming.<br /><br />Which I think is the whole point. <br /><br />Ever since I was fifteen, I promised myself I would never get into a relationship with someone before I knew what they looked like angry. Are they the type to grow exasperated and leave the room, shout their lungs out or… aggressively hit their loved ones?<br /><br />I’m very happy with the way Colleen Hoover dealt with the subject of abuse. It’s very well explored and the connection between Lily and her mother so beautiful yet so sad. But mostly beautiful because of how well they end up understanding one another.<br /><br />To be completely honest, I wanted to stay way away from this book. The last CoHo books I had read – UGLY LOVE and NOVEMBER 9 – annoyed me with their cheesy lines and insta-love-dovey. But this… this is something else entirely. <br /><br />I loved how it follows Lily for several years and how we even get access to her past. It not only made her character much more three-dimensional—real, but it also showed sides of her we otherwise would never have seen. She is so strong and wise. So motivated and ambitious. So good and compassionate. I loved her. And truth be told, I want to be her.<br /><br />I think this book has truly renewed my faith in Colleen Hoover. I almost gave up on reading her books for ever, but then impulsion struck me and I succumbed to this one as well. Very glad I did. I hope you will, too. It’s worth it. <br /><br />PS. The title is one of the most well thought of that exist. When the author used the sentence in her novel, all kinds of emotions welled up inside me. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a><br /></span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1834084206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9491559657636489139">If you need me I'll be sweeping up all the pieces of my shattered heart. Dear God! It's amazing how you can read a story that is simultaneously gut wrenching and beautiful. I'll be honest, I managed to make it through this ENTIRE book without shedding a single tear... until I hit CoHo's note/acknowledgements at the end and ugly cried. The fact that this story had so much basis on real life events that meant so much to her shined through in her writing. <br/><br/>Clearly you can guess the ending of the sto</span>
  <span id="freeText9491559657636489139" style="display:none">If you need me I'll be sweeping up all the pieces of my shattered heart. Dear God! It's amazing how you can read a story that is simultaneously gut wrenching and beautiful. I'll be honest, I managed to make it through this ENTIRE book without shedding a single tear... until I hit CoHo's note/acknowledgements at the end and ugly cried. The fact that this story had so much basis on real life events that meant so much to her shined through in her writing. <br /><br />Clearly you can guess the ending of the story (to some degree) by the title, but a majority of what makes this story so breathtaking is the journey there. "It Ends With Us" caused me to look at domestic abuse in ways I never allowed myself to in the past. As a society we are quick to judge women (and men) who stay in abusive relationships without taking into account what the process really is like for them. We get a slight glimpse into the fragile situation of how incredibly difficult it is to leave a dangerous relationship when you love the person who is causing you harm. I won't say more for fear of ruining the reading experience for someone else, but this book was so much more than a flimsy romance novel. Highly recommended! (Maybe I'll stop ugly crying by the time you've finished reading it.)</span>

<div id="review_1570392733" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1570392733" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1570392733?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Katerina by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/30934456">Τατιάνα Τζινιώλη</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1570392733" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7519514097138010817"><b>I honestly don't know how I feel.</b><br/><br/>There are times I am <b>angry</b> and times I am <b>sad</b>. And then I'm both. And it's the worst, because there is a war raging inside me, and the winner side keeps changing. How is it possible to switch from denial to sorrow to fury to acceptance in a heartbeat?<br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“There is no such thing as bad people. We’re all just people who sometimes do bad things.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>I did my best not to cry. I felt sick, but I clenched my jaw and forced myself to keep reading, trying in vain to</span>
  <span id="freeText7519514097138010817" style="display:none"><b>I honestly don't know how I feel.</b><br /><br />There are times I am <b>angry</b> and times I am <b>sad</b>. And then I'm both. And it's the worst, because there is a war raging inside me, and the winner side keeps changing. How is it possible to switch from denial to sorrow to fury to acceptance in a heartbeat?<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“There is no such thing as bad people. We’re all just people who sometimes do bad things.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />I did my best not to cry. I felt sick, but I clenched my jaw and forced myself to keep reading, trying in vain to ignore the tremors that ran through my body. But when the last chapters came, and Colleen's note in the end, I couldn't take it any more. I dissolved into angry, hot tears, and I checked my chest to make sure my heart was not bleeding. Lily's story had a lot to teach. I think I died a little when I realized that sometimes <b>love is not enough</b>. Regret, good will, they're not enough to fix some wounds. On the contrary, they make them deeper.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Just because someone hurts you doesn't mean you can simply stop loving them. It's not a person's actions that hurt the most. It's the love. If there was no love attached to the action, the pain would be a little easier to bear.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27362503.It_Ends_with_Us" title="It Ends with Us by Colleen Hoover" rel="nofollow noopener">It Ends with Us</a> is the most personal and daring and painful book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5430144.Colleen_Hoover" title="Colleen Hoover" rel="nofollow noopener">Colleen Hoover</a> has ever written. Abuse</b> and <b>domestic violence</b> are a delicate subject, and when I found out they were this book's main theme I thought about not reading it. It was a moment of cowardice, a moment I didn't want to witness this side of relationships. But I owed it to myself, as a person and as a woman to proceed. Because pretending a problem doesn't exist does not make it disappear. There will be <b>spoilers </b>below so if you haven't read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27362503.It_Ends_with_Us" title="It Ends with Us by Colleen Hoover" rel="nofollow noopener">It Ends with Us</a>, you should probably stop here.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Fifteen seconds. That’s all it takes to completely change everything about a person. Fifteen.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Naked truth coming. I was one of the people who don't understand. The people who, when they hear about abuse, the first thing that occurs to them is <i>why doesn't <b>she</b> leave him? Why does she let her fear guide her, and she's so selfish that makes her children witness such horrors inside their home, that was supposed to be their sanctuary?</i> But what we should ask is <i>what is wrong with <b>him</b>?</i> Instead of making excuses and trying to justify him, we should take a moment and consider how she feels, and the difficult decisions she has to make. <b>Ryle broke my heart into millions of pieces. </b>I fell in love with him, and I kept wishing that Colleen would delete these words, these scenes that hurt me and disappointed me and shattered my belief in happy endings. A part of me, a part I tried to smother, a part I am ashamed that exists, wanted him to change. To try harder, and for Lily to let him try harder. Me, who judged them for not leaving. In the end, <b>I felt sorry for Ryle</b>. For losing the love of his life, for destroying his only chance at happiness. I don't forgive him, I just wish that a magic wand would make everything better.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“So much gravity, pushing down on my emotions. Everything shatters.<br />My tears, my heart, my laughter, my soul. Shattered like broken glass, raining down around me.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><b>Lily is a hero.</b> She had <b>dignity</b>, and <b>courage</b> and <b>strength</b>. At first I was judging her mother for staying, but witnessing through Lily's eyes her challenges, feeling her heartbreak and her dilemmas, made me regret all the ugly things I thought. Loving the person who hurts you is a greater torture than the physical act itself. And damn it I loved Ryle, and I hated Colleen for that. <b>I hated her for making me swoon and laugh when she was about to shatter my soul. </b>The Katerina that started <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27362503.It_Ends_with_Us" title="It Ends with Us by Colleen Hoover" rel="nofollow noopener">It Ends with Us</a> is a different person than the Katerina that finished it. Remorseful, destroyed, wiser.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Life is a funny thing. We only get so many years to live it, so we have to do everything we can to make sure those years are as full as they can be. We shouldn't waste time on things that might happen someday, or maybe even never.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />A part of me wants to forget this <b>raw, powerful, inspirational, beautiful and ugly book</b>. But the dominant part, even though it suffers, is glad I read it and learned.<br />To every single person out there, <b>READ IT</b>.<br />To every woman in Lily's place, <b>BE BRAVE AND BOLD</b>.<br />To <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5430144.Colleen_Hoover" title="Colleen Hoover" rel="nofollow noopener">Colleen Hoover</a>, <b>THANK YOU</b>. For sharing this with us. With me.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Just keep swimming.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><i></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7519514097138010817" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2301958402" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2301958402" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2301958402?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2018">z-read2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2016">y-out2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2018">z-faves2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-coverporn">z-coverporn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=genre-experiments">genre-experiments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=trauma-abuse-recovery">trauma-abuse-recovery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=she-did-that">she-did-that</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2301958402" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4752951686650069056">You guys are always telling me this author writes vaguely shitty romance novels and is unbelievably overhyped... and yet this masterpiece exists? I call bullshit because this was masterful.<br/><br/>If you have read this book and also follow my reviews, you know the topic of abuse is one I sort of talk about a lot. this book got it right. this book got it so, so right. <b>
  <u>So let’s talk about why.</u>
</b><br/><br/><i>
  <b>→ character work ←</b>
</i><br/>I knew I would love Lily from the moment she stood up at her abusive father’s funeral an</span>
  <span id="freeText4752951686650069056" style="display:none">You guys are always telling me this author writes vaguely shitty romance novels and is unbelievably overhyped... and yet this masterpiece exists? I call bullshit because this was masterful.<br /><br />If you have read this book and also follow my reviews, you know the topic of abuse is one I sort of talk about a lot. this book got it right. this book got it so, so right. <b>
  <u>So let’s talk about why.</u>
</b><br /><br /><i>
  <b>→ character work ←</b>
</i><br />I knew I would love Lily from the moment she stood up at her abusive father’s funeral and refused to speak. And oh boy, was I right. Lily works so well as a protagonist because she <i>isn’t</i> the archetype. She has been through abuse herself and she is so, so sure it would never happen to her. She would leave if even one thing happened. She would. ...But then she doesn’t. She reads as absolutely, totally real. And her character development? Fucking iconic. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>→ friendship focus ←</b>
</i><br />Something that really bothers me a lot in romances like this is that a romance tends to <i>save</i> the protagonist, and I think this book - despite marketing that made me concerned this trope would rear its ugly head - <b>
  <u>does the opposite.</u>
</b> The lead friendship here between Lily and Alys is so 20/10 and so <i>important</i>. And even though there <i>is</i> a touch of romance, I think the book is very explicit about it <b>not being healthy for Lily to jump right into a new relationship.</b> I appreciate that a lot. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>→ narrative treatment ←</b>
</i><br />I think this is one of the only books I have ever read that actually seems to understand that <b>
  <u>abuse is a mortal sin.</u>
</b> The wild thing is, aside from his moments of extreme rage, Rylin never appears to be <i>that</i> bad of a guy. He apologizes every time. He continuously seems to account for Lily’s feelings. But his actions against her are <i>enough</i>. There is no question in the narrative on whether she was being unempathetic: Lily was <i>right</i> to leave, no matter how he treated her in the aftermath. And I think that means a lot to me, how his character is nuanced but also irredeemable for Lily. <br /><br />I mean, aside from these three things, everything about this novel was basically good - the writing is extremely clean and easy-to-read, there are some really really funny moments, the romance that <i>does</i> end up occurring is genuinely sweet, and it's overall a win - but on a personal level? I am destroyed. This book is not just good, this book is Fantastic. and that's my opinion. goodnight. <br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4752951686650069056" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
