<div id="review_1634841043" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1634841043" />
    <a title="alexandra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6784858-alexandra"><img alt="alexandra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592456461p2/6784858.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1634841043?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="alexandra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="alexandra" href="/user/show/6784858-alexandra">alexandra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6784858-alexandra?shelf=frustration">frustration</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6784858-alexandra?shelf=influential">influential</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6784858-alexandra?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6784858-alexandra?shelf=ss">ss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1634841043" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13725669479087250067">2.5/5 ♡ this book sends a really important and worthwhile message, but it's not necessarily enjoyable.<br/><br/>IT ENDS WITH US was not what i expected it to be. i started the novel knowing next to nothing about the storyline except that it's a colleen hoover book (NA romance) and that it's <em>good</em> (my friends kept raving). but if i'm being honest, i was a little disappointed. i was hoping for a light read with lots of ~FEELZ~ but instead i got something much more intense – not bad, just unexpected.<br/><br/>the main </span>
  <span id="freeText13725669479087250067" style="display:none">2.5/5 ♡ this book sends a really important and worthwhile message, but it's not necessarily enjoyable.<br /><br />IT ENDS WITH US was not what i expected it to be. i started the novel knowing next to nothing about the storyline except that it's a colleen hoover book (NA romance) and that it's <em>good</em> (my friends kept raving). but if i'm being honest, i was a little disappointed. i was hoping for a light read with lots of ~FEELZ~ but instead i got something much more intense – not bad, just unexpected.<br /><br />the main plot revolves around abusive and toxic relationships within families. it really opened my eyes to the emotions of those in these types of situations and helped me gain a lot of perspective. because of this, i think it's important for everyone to read this, but i can't say if you'll like it.<br /><br />for the majority of this novel, i DIDN'T like it. i was definitely interested and curious, but i didn't care for the characters as much as i thought i would. i was frustrated and annoyed at the situations, and some of it felt artificial, rushed, and sterotypical. it all seemed so... fictional. usually the romance satisfies me, but even that didn't do it. buuuuuut it wasn't so much that i didn't NOT like it. it was simply okay when i expected it to be ~amazing~.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />there were two romantic tropes that bothered me because i don't like the tropes themselves and because i didn't think it was executed THAT well: insta-love and love triangle. <br /><br />ryle was too good to be true; a hot, young, smart, compassionate, arrogant, sensitive, rich guy suddenly appears and falls head over heels for our main character. they – somehow!! – meet again and this time he's literally BEGGING to have sex with her. suddenly, this fuckboi wants to be in a committed relationship and plans on having kids with our lucky lady. um......... okay????? i didn't feel anything for their relationship and ryle seemed like a plot device to me. and when she didn't leave him the first time, i knew i KNEW he would do much worse again. and i didn't feel surprised when it happened; i didn't feel surprised when she asked for the divorce – a little relieved maybe, but not surprised.<br /><br />then there's atlas, who i felt had more depth than ryle and lily but also not thaaaat much. he was probably my favorite character, but i felt his story (the letters) were kinda.. anti-climactic? their relationship was confusing to decipher, but i still loved them. it made me sad to think lily didn't end up with atlas IN THE FIRST PLACE but i guess that would make the whole purpose of the book redundant.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />even though i didn't enjoy the process of reading this book, i'm grateful to have read it. there are some books you read for pleasure and there are some you read to gain knowledge and perspective. this is the latter.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13725669479087250067" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1716662574" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1716662574" />
    <a title="Noel Luis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58194738-noel-luis"><img alt="Noel Luis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557585199p2/58194738.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1716662574?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Noel Luis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Noel Luis" href="/user/show/58194738-noel-luis">Noel Luis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58194738-noel-luis?shelf=above-average">above-average</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1716662574" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7897987843298551478"><b>SPOILER FREE REVIEW</b><br/><br/>As a member of the human species with a Y chromosome, I admit that the allure of the romance novel eludes me, even though I'm a particularly hopeless romantic myself. The thought of reading about a prolonged courtship isn't something to get all excited about. After all, how many people out there are actually interested in hearing about my own misadventures in the dating arena?<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470152200ra/19895098.gif' alt='worst-dating' width='416' height='310' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>On second thought, don't answer that.<br/><br/>So when I started diving into <em>It Ends with Us: A Novel</em> by Colleen</span>
  <span id="freeText7897987843298551478" style="display:none"><b>SPOILER FREE REVIEW</b><br><br>As a member of the human species with a Y chromosome, I admit that the allure of the romance novel eludes me, even though I'm a particularly hopeless romantic myself. The thought of reading about a prolonged courtship isn't something to get all excited about. After all, how many people out there are actually interested in hearing about my own misadventures in the dating arena?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470152200ra/19895098.gif" alt="worst-dating" width="416" height="310" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>On second thought, don't answer that.<br><br>So when I started diving into <em>It Ends with Us: A Novel</em> by Colleen Hoover, I expected pages of the same old trite that have filled thousands of romance novels ever since the first caveman dragged the first cavechick by the hair back into his stone-age pad. Wouldn't you know it? I wasn't disappointed in the slightest. Let's take a brief rundown of the requisite elements and see if this novel has them:<br> <br> 	 Girl Meets Boy - CHECK <br> 	 Boy is Impossibly Handsome - CHECK <br> 	 Boy is Impossibly Rich - CHECK <br> 	 Boy is Impossibly Talented - CHECK <br> 	 Boy has Mysterious Name - CHECK <br> 	 Boy is Emotionally Aloof - CHECK <br> 	 Girl Tries To Deny Feelings For Boy She Just Met - CHECK <br> 	 Boy Makes A Move - CHECK <br> 	 Girl Pretends Not To Like It - CHECK <br> 	 Boy Says Something Clever and Sexy - CHECK <br> 	 Boy and Girl Have Wild, Raunchy Sex - CHECK <br> <br>Okay, the last one actually doesn't happen for a good while owing to the tried-and-tested phone-call-interruption-just-when-we're-about-to-do-it cliche, but it's still there.<br><br>Here's a description of when the two lovebirds first meet:<br><blockquote>I feel his voice in my stomach. That's not good. Voices should stop at the ears, but sometimes - not very often at all, actually - a voice will penetrate past my ears and reverberate straight down through my body. He has one of those voices. Deep, confident, and a little bit like butter.</blockquote><br><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470152200ra/19895099.gif" alt="butter-for-me" width="480" height="267" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><br>Here's another one:<br><blockquote>This guy is beautiful. Well-manicured, smells like money, looks to be several years older than me. His eyes crinkle in the corners as they follow me, and his lips seem to frown, even when they aren't.</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470152200ra/19895100.gif" alt="wink" width="500" height="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now, why would I give four stars to a book that overuses so many tropes?<br><br>Because Colleen Hoover knows her audience so well it's almost criminal. Her writing is clean and lucid. The protagonist is fleshed-out. The story tugs at the heart. Everything else can be forgiven.<br><br>And by the end of the first half of the book, it becomes painfully obvious that this novel is not about romance. It's about heartache.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470152200ra/19895101.gif" alt="broken-heart" width="500" height="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Our protagonist is a 23-year old wannabe florist named Lily Blossom Bloom (yes) who meets brooding neurosurgeon Ryle Kincaid (again, yes). Lily's father has recently passed, and she's trying to come to terms with her less-than-stellar relationship with dear ol' dad. Flashbacks are interspersed throughout the book via Lily's high school diary, and we quickly find out that her first love was a homeless guy named Atlas Corrigan (for the last time, yes) who lived in an abandoned shack near her childhood home. To say that dad and Atlas did not get along is an understatement.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470152200i/19895102._SY540_.png" alt="the-rock" width="500" height="616" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Lily is a smart and driven woman, and it shows through her personality. She balances the pleasures of love with the pleasures of work. A couple chapters in, she decides to pursue her dream and open a flower shop:<br><blockquote>"Sweet, life, pink, spring." I repeat. And then, "Allysa, you're brilliant!" I stand up and begin pacing the floor. "We'll take everything everyone loves about flowers, and we'll do the complete opposite!"</blockquote><br>Nice one, Lily.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470152200ra/19895103.gif" alt="genius" width="350" height="197" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But of course, this wouldn't be a good novel if all we ever read about is how good Lily is getting it at the office and in the bedroom. Midway through, disaster strikes.<br><br>I won't say what kind of disaster, but there's quite a few of it, both in present time and in the flashbacks. And then there's love. And then there's disaster. And then there's love. And then there's disaster. And then there's love.<br><br>This book may overuse so many things we've come to expect of romantic comedies, but when I figured out the real message Colleen wanted to impart, I swept all the small things under the rug. This novel is a heartfelt plea for the readers to empathize with men and women who are caught up in relationships that are causing them turmoil and pain. It's a call to have an open mind when confronted with a similar relationship in the real world, both for the man, the woman, and their families. Finally, it leaves us with a beautiful if not sad moral lesson that the right thing to do may sometimes also be the hardest thing to do.<br><blockquote>People say that teenagers don't know how to love like an adult. Part of me believes that, but I'm not an adult so I have nothing to compare it to. But I do believe it's probably different. I'm sure there's more substance in the love between two adults than there is between two teenagers. There's probably more maturity, more respect, more responsibility. But no matter how different the substance of a love might be at different ages in a person's life, I know that love still has to weigh the same. You feel that weight on your shoulders and in your stomach and on your heart no matter how old you are.</blockquote><br>The book is peppered with phrases like the one above, and the more I read, the more I got the feeling that the words were coming from the author's mouth and not the protagonist's.<br><br>At the beginning and end of the novel, there is a personal message left by the author, and the motivation for this book suddenly becomes clear. They say writing is a private and cathartic process, and for Colleen, this certainly was extremely private and cathartic. It must have taken a lot of effort to write. It's only fair that it took a lot of joy to read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7897987843298551478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1785971543" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1785971543" />
    <a title="The Burning Rose (Jess)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess"><img alt="The Burning Rose (Jess)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605317941p2/48477217.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1785971543?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Burning Rose (Jess)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Burning Rose (Jess)" href="/user/show/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess">The Burning Rose (Jess)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781501110368" href="/book/show/27276318-it-ends-with-us">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1785971543" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11300466200526785756">5/5 incredible stars.<br/>Colleen Hoover strikes again.<br/>This book has completely misled me, I admit.<br/>This is actually the third book I read from this writer. I don't remember much of the first book (Ugly Love), but I'm aware that I loved it. I think I'll read it again soon, to refresh things.<br/>Then, I read the book "Confession." That's where I fell in love. And strongly. I don't know if you read my review of this book, but if so, I guess you can notice how much this book has affected me.<br/>Anyway, the name </span>
  <span id="freeText11300466200526785756" style="display:none">5/5 incredible stars.<br />Colleen Hoover strikes again.<br />This book has completely misled me, I admit.<br />This is actually the third book I read from this writer. I don't remember much of the first book (Ugly Love), but I'm aware that I loved it. I think I'll read it again soon, to refresh things.<br />Then, I read the book "Confession." That's where I fell in love. And strongly. I don't know if you read my review of this book, but if so, I guess you can notice how much this book has affected me.<br />Anyway, the name "Colleen Hoover" was engraved in my head, and I came to the decision that I wanted to read more of her books. I admit I didn't really know which book to pick up, so I did it randomly. I have to admit, the impression I got about this book from the description is not wow. But if that's what I got, then whatever.<br />Now I thank my random choice, and big time.<br />Like I said, this book fooled me.<br />I was sure at the beginning that it was such a nice love book. Oh, how wrong I was.<br />Continuing, I realized how amazing Colleen Hoover is, how fascinating this book is, and how important the message and meaning is.<br /><br />This isn’t a book that tells only about love, it is a book about the lives of quite a few women in the world who have experienced it.<br />The plot talks about Lily, a sweet girl who tried hard to rearrange her life.<br />At the beginning of the book, she meets Ryle, a smart, handsome, assertive neurosurgeon. And he really likes Lily.<br />They manage to connect and get to know each other with their secrets. They call it "naked truth." The extraordinary truths and familiarity brought them to life together. But how can you forget the sweet guy from Lily's past?<br />Atlas is an absolutely exceptional guy. The book bounces you between the past, written from Lily's diary, to the present. In her diary, Lily talks about Atlas, a child without a home, without a family. Lily helps Atlas, she sneaks him to her house, lets him take a shower, gives him clothes, watch TV together, eat, talk, get to know each other. The connection between them is definitely special. But I guess everything has an end- or... doesn't it?<br />When Lily and Ryle enter an upscale restaurant, Lily encounters Atlas, after so many years, and discovers that he has managed to create and bring his life to a good place.<br />Sounds like a cliche love story to you, right?<br />So it's not.<br />I don't want to do spoilers, so I would be very careful. it’s a book about strong love, with problems that quite a few women get into a cruel situation. There are women who manage to take their feet and walk, and some do not.<br />Our main character, Lily, who is indeed a special hero for me, is going through jolts, ups and downs. Will her love succeed in overcoming logic? Or could logic make it better for her love? <br /><br />You know, a lot of people tend to say, "Oh, come on, to me it won't happen, I'll never get to that."<br />Well, it might not. But it can be. Whether it's a man or a woman - whether you're on the violent or innocent side. You can get into that kind of situation. We all can.<br />This is a book that should reach a wide audience - men, women, adults and more. This is a book that teaches a terribly important lesson in life.<br />You know, I learned about that in psychology and sociology. Freud talked about it - it's called a defense mechanism.<br />This is a situation where the person starts to make a “rationalization”. It operates by the subconscious mind. The person may even not be openly aware of it, but only in the subconscious. It is very difficult, and I can talk about it for hours, but I can’t do it here lol.<br />To sum up, that’s why this book is so important.<br /><br />So of course I highly recommend this book. Have a good read, my loves.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11300466200526785756" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2084365810" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2084365810" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2084365810?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2084365810" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1315738526089366693"><i>”Oh, I want you, Lily. Make no mistake about that. I just don’t want to want you.”</i> <br/><br/>I thought really long and hard about how I’m going to review this book and what it always comes down to, is that I actually don’t want to review it. <br/><br/>This is one of the rare books you just have to read yourself. You have to experience it and feel it and no matter what I’d write in my review, it would never even get close to all the emotions that hit me while I read <b>“It Ends With Us”</b>. This book makes you happy and s</span>
  <span id="freeText1315738526089366693" style="display:none"><i>”Oh, I want you, Lily. Make no mistake about that. I just don’t want to want you.”</i> <br /><br />I thought really long and hard about how I’m going to review this book and what it always comes down to, is that I actually don’t want to review it. <br /><br />This is one of the rare books you just have to read yourself. You have to experience it and feel it and no matter what I’d write in my review, it would never even get close to all the emotions that hit me while I read <b>“It Ends With Us”</b>. This book makes you happy and sad, it confuses you, breaks you, hurts you, makes you question yourself and your thoughts! Hell, it makes you question your own code of ethics. <br /><br /><i>”The reasoning is the hardest part of this. It eats at me, little by little, wearing down the strength my hatred lends to me.”</i><br /><br />It would be easy to judge; easy to sit on a high horse, but the way this is written, the way Colleen Hoover conveyed her feelings… It makes it impossible to go out of this book without acknowledging her POV, it makes it impossible not to think about it. I know the world is not white and black. I always knew that there are many shades of grey, but this book? It confronts you with the deepest grey and forces you to deal with it. It poses the simple question: What would I have done? <br /><br />And as usually, the simple questions of life are the hardest and most complicated to answer. ;-)<br /><br /><i>”All humans make mistakes. What determines a person’s character aren’t the mistakes we make. It’s how we take those mistakes and turn them into lessons rather than excuses.”</i><br /><br />We all know what we <b>SHOULD</b> do in certain situations! What is expected of us, but when you’re actually in one of those situations? When feelings are involved? It’s not that easy anymore…<br />I could be vague and probably continue like that forever but I won’t say more than this! It wouldn’t be fair to all the people who still want to read <b>“It Ends With Us”</b>. <br /><br />So all I’m saying is this:<br /><br />- This book is important! <br />- I really liked Lily as a character and I admire her! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[She did the right thing in a very difficult situation and she was so, so, so brave to end her relationship with Ryle!!! It had to be done, for the sake of her child, she had not only to let go of him but also of her hatred <b>for</b> him. And to reach that point, to make that decision, to give her child the opportunity to have a father and to forgive him for what he did? THAT WOMAN IS STRONG!!! &lt;333 She has all my love and being a mother myself who only wants the best for her child, I could understand her decision!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />- Atlas is a precious bean and I love that man! &lt;3 <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>”I close my eyes as I soak up the familiarity of him. His smell, his touch, his comfort. I’ve never understood how someone can be so rock solid, yet comforting. But that’s always how I viewed him. Like he could withstand anything, but somehow still feels the weight that everyone else carries.”</i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />- I enjoyed the two different POVs from Lily. Her teenage diary entries and the current plot made this a really intriguing read. Sometimes it felt like there were two different Lily’s which dominated the story line and I guess in some way there were, because the years of experience made them two different people. <br />- Alyssa was the best friend ever!!! &lt;33 <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When she told Lily that as her brother’s sister she didn’t want her to leave him but that as her best friend she had to tell her that she HAD to leave him, I actually had tears in my eyes! I loved her for saying this! Because she knew that Lily couldn’t be with Ryle and she loved her enough to help her to make the right decision. And this even though Ryle was her brother!! It takes strength not to let those family bonds get in the way and Issa was a very strong character for sure.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />- The ending…. I’ll never get over it. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I really liked Ryle at the beginning of the book but the first time he hit her, I already wanted her to leave him. To hit your wife is inexcusable, to hit her twice or three times? Unforgivable! <br /> <i>”You are my wife. I’m supposed to be the one who protects you from the monsters. I’m not supposed to be one.”</i><br />I really wish I would have found out why Ryle was the way he was, I mean I get that the death of his brother did something with him, but why could he be so nice and caring to his sister and his own child, but felt an urge to hit his wife? Just because he was angry and saw red? For me as an outsider this is kind of tough to understand. A Ryle POV might have helped to understand him better. I mean it was obvious he regretted what he did, that he knew it was wrong, that he wished he would have never done it and that he hated himself for it. But WHY????!!!! WHY, Ryle??!! I guess that’s the main reason why I’m still thinking about this book. I’m having a difficult time to understand his actions, but maybe I’m just overthinking it and he really had no control over what he did… I guess I’ll never know. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />- Read it, but be warned! It’s not an easy read. Trigger warnings: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[domestic abuse, violence against women, abusive relationships, homelessness <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Conclusion:</b><br /><br />This was an emotional and haunting read and totally not what I expected. It definitely kept me on my toes though. XD Colleen Hoover is a great author and I’ll continue to read her other books. In future I just might be a little bit more careful when I start one of them. ;-)<br /><br />___________________________________<br /><br />It was time to consult my <a href="https://thesassylibraryfox.wordpress.com/2018/11/11/the-curse-of-cheap-e-books/" rel="nofollow noopener">"Bookie Jar"</a> and to find out what I should read next.<br /><br />Apparently it wants me to read my first Colleen Hoover book ever and I’m so ready for it.<br />I’ve seen her books all over my feed and I’m very curious if I’ll like “It Ends With Us”.<br /><br />I didn’t read many romances lately and I’m really no expert when it comes to this particular kind of genre, so I’m definitely open for it. So far the only romance authors I can recommend are Joyo Moyes, Cecilia Ahern and Nicolas Sparks. *lol*<br /><br />Let’s find out if I’ll be able to recommend Colleen Hoover in future too. ;-P</span>
  <a data-text-id="1315738526089366693" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1162396021" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1162396021" />
    <a title="Andreea Pop" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4858513-andreea-pop"><img alt="Andreea Pop" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486663526p2/4858513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1162396021?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andreea Pop" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andreea Pop" href="/user/show/4858513-andreea-pop">Andreea Pop</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=cry-the-shit-out-of-me">cry-the-shit-out-of-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=i-worship-these">i-worship-these</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=love-it-but-hate-it">love-it-but-hate-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=non-fantasy">non-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=real-life-problems">real-life-problems</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=badass-heroine">badass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=amazing-feelings">amazing-feelings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1162396021" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14510234114071313838"><i>
  <b>“There is no such thing as bad people. We’re all just people who sometimes do bad things.” </b>
</i><br/><br/><b>I am</b> a mess. Torn. So, so goddamn conflicted. Broken over the what-ifs of this book. Filled with sorrow. Proud. <br/><br/><b>I feel</b> manipulated. Tricked. Heartbroken. Educated. Thankful. Mindfucked. <br/><br/><i>It Ends With Us</i> is nothing like I’ve ever read. It certainly isn’t like any other novel Colleen Hoover has written. The word ‘DIFFERENT’ is just etched into its very essence. I feel like Colleen put part of her story an</span>
  <span id="freeText14510234114071313838" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“There is no such thing as bad people. We’re all just people who sometimes do bad things.” </b>
</i><br><br><b>I am</b> a mess. Torn. So, so goddamn conflicted. Broken over the what-ifs of this book. Filled with sorrow. Proud. <br><br><b>I feel</b> manipulated. Tricked. Heartbroken. Educated. Thankful. Mindfucked. <br><br><i>It Ends With Us</i> is nothing like I’ve ever read. It certainly isn’t like any other novel Colleen Hoover has written. The word ‘DIFFERENT’ is just etched into its very essence. I feel like Colleen put part of her story and her soul on a silver platter for us to observe and draw our own conclusions from it and this also became evident within the Author’s Note which, by the way, I wholeheartedly encourage you to read. Hell, no. Scratch that. <b>I WHOLEHEARTEDLY ENCOURAGE YOU TO READ IT ENDS WITH US</b>. Not because of the hype. Not because of the romance. Not because of Colleen’s awesome writing skills. <br><br>But because of <i>the message</i>. <br><br>I cannot guarantee you’ll love it. I’m definitely far from loving it and I don’t even think it’s Colleen’s best work. This is the second book that’s ever made me feel the ‘I-love-it-but-I-hate-it’ vibes, the first being <i>Dusty</i>. I rated that one with 3 stars because based on my logic 1 star equals hate and 5 stars equate to love so the average of 3 will do. But I rated IEWU with a full 5 stars rating because if there’s one word to describe this book, then it’s <b>EMPOWERING.</b> And WOMEN EMPOWERMENT deserves 5 stars any given day. Plus, its unraveling is perfect.<br><br>Without being spoilery, I will say this: this book is heavy. This book knifes your heart and twists it until you bleed all your pre-conceived ideas about certain topics straight out the window. I loved Lily. I loved Ryle. But most of all, <u>I loved Lily &amp; Ryle</u>. Their relationship is so complex and layered and I was overwhelmed with feelings at just how perfect they were together. I laughed, I smiled, I felt my heart catch wings and head into the clouds. And then I cried buckets. Then there’s Atlas, which I did not fall in love with, but he just fit the puzzle perfectly and after a while I found him so lovable as well. And yes, I loved Lily &amp; Atlas too. They were like a weak but brilliant rainbow after a storm.<br><br><i>
  <b>“In the future . . . if by some miracle you ever find yourself in the position to fall in love again . . . fall in love with me.” </b>
</i><br><br>Now, now, don’t rush and believe this is some love triangle. I just feel evil now and I will say that <b>YOU HAVE NO FUCKING IDEA MUHAHA.</b> <i>*sobs*</i><br><br>I’m not saying more because you should definitely head in blind with this one, as I did. Honorary mentions are needed, however: <b>Alyssa</b>, I swear, she’s the best friend I could possibly imagine; I cannot comprehend how difficult it must have been to say and do some things considering the unique dynamics of her with the other characters; <b>Marshall</b> was another great addition that simply showed how easily men can empower women too; and <b>Lily’s mother</b> is a glorious character. <br><br>And I will share this: there was one particular scene that left me crying like there’s no tomorrow. The last hospital scene. <b>That beautiful and so very ugly and just 100% gut-wrenching scene.</b> Where decisions were made in the hopes of a better future. Where letting go was worth the love you’ve built piece by piece. Where the cycle of history stopped. Where I had to put the book down and start a sobfest. It gutted me, completely and utterly gutted me. <br><br><i>
  <b>“And as hard as this choice is, we break the pattern before the pattern breaks us.”</b>
</i><br><br>I read this book in 5 hours. I finished it 24 hours ago. I still can’t stop thinking about it and my stomach is still churning like ashes have taken residence there. I’m an emotional mess. I feel unsatisfied, yet content. Enraged, yet peaceful. This book shows the good, the bad, the in-between. It shows life and love and hatred. It shows how love can become a poison. It shows how love can shackle and hurt, but also save and heal. Honestly, it blew my mind. It doesn’t matter that it made me uncomfortable or that it made me wish things ended up differently. <b>This story needed to exist exactly as it is no matter how broken my heart feels. It is brave and bold.</b><br><br><b>It’s an eye-opener.</b> I realized upon reading that I might have been indifferent or dismissive or downright judgmental regarding some <i>statistics</i> (this sounds weird, I know, but you’ll get it once you read). I never fully grasped some scenarios or some perspectives, but <i>It Ends With Us</i> changed that. It changed me, undoubtedly. <br><br>And for that, thank you, Colleen. Thank you, Lily. <b>Thank you for making me a better person. <br><br><a href="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-d74gBHdbnAQ/V7MUKYRli-I/AAAAAAAAQW8/bnjFYcSM8a4Xe5rkIBtk_W01Mod9FP_JgCLcB/s1600/13934756_1371818922831705_364108687886398105_n.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener"><img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471353917i/20034655.jpg" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14510234114071313838" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1423669578" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1423669578" />
    <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee"><img alt="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583262285p2/44137919.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1423669578?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee">Mikee (ReadWithMikee)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781501110368" href="/book/show/27276318-it-ends-with-us">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1423669578" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17676772113118455624"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470308538i/19912154._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Find me on <a href='http://www.instagram.com/readwithmikee' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> & <a href='http://www.twitter.com/readwithmikee' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a>!<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>❝I wish cutting my feelings off for the person who hurt me was as easy as I used to think it would be. Preventing your heart from forgiving someone you love is actually a hell of a lot harder than simply forgiving them.❞</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>It Ends With Us was beautifully complicated. It was hot and cold. Up and down. Good and bad. Beautiful and ugly... I'm still trying to figure out how I really feel about it all because I'm genuinely torn on how I want to perceive this st</span>
  <span id="freeText17676772113118455624" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470308538i/19912154._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Find me on <a href="http://www.instagram.com/readwithmikee" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> &amp; <a href="http://www.twitter.com/readwithmikee" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a>!<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>❝I wish cutting my feelings off for the person who hurt me was as easy as I used to think it would be. Preventing your heart from forgiving someone you love is actually a hell of a lot harder than simply forgiving them.❞</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>It Ends With Us was beautifully complicated. It was hot and cold. Up and down. Good and bad. Beautiful and ugly... I'm still trying to figure out how I really feel about it all because I'm genuinely torn on how I want to perceive this storyline. I loved it but in all honesty, I really do think I hate it as well. Not the "I-hate-you-Colleen-Hoover-stop-writing-books-and-find-a-different-career" type of hate but rather "I-hate-you-Colleen-Hoover-for-making-me-hate-everything-that-I-came-to-love" kind of hate because it pretty much summarizes all my thoughts and feelings about It Ends With Us in one sentence.<br><br>My opinions were completely divided. One side of me, the hopeless romantic, was utterly unsatisfied and angry with the outcome of the story. The opposite side, the one that's all about women's empowerment, was cheering on #TeamLily like it was Independence Day.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br>Rather than trying to sugarcoat my thoughts, I'm just going to be completely honest. I was 100 percent team Ryle from the very first time we met him. Just like Lily, I fell in love with every word and every gesture that rolled off of his body. I. WAS. HOOKED. It also didn't help that I kept fantasizing Doctor Mike as Ryle Kincaid. *heart eyes emoji* I loved his ambition. His personality. His confidence. To be honest, I think I might've loved Ryle even more than Lily did but that's another story for another day. That more than likely explains why I took the second half of this book like a blow to the gut.<br><br>Once we got to the second half of the book, that's where it started going a bit downhill for me as a Ryle and Lily shipper. Every happy moment that ever happened between my ship came barreling down as it collided with pain and abuse. I was angry. I was thrashing. I was yelling at the pages in front of me, "Why are you doing this Colleen?!" But most importantly, I was just heartbroken to see such a beautiful couple become so toxic. Everything I loved about the first half of the book was slowly unraveling right before my very eyes as if it never really existed in the first place. I can't even remember how many times I wanted to put the book down because my hopeless romantic self just couldn't handle it anymore. But I just kept on reading because I was guiltily hoping that Ryle and Lily would still have their happy ending despite all that had happened. :/ Sadly, this was where I was torn the most.<br><br>I have the upmost respect for Lily. She is definitely one of my favorite female characters that Colleen has ever created because she did what a lot of us would've struggled to do in the end: walk away. Lily was such a strong character and I admire her so much for having the strength to stand up for herself. There were numerous times towards the end of the book where I knew I probably would've gave in and forgave Ryle for his actions but Lily was inflexible. She was in a tough position but she put her foot down and demanded better for herself. In the end, no matter if I ship Ryle/Lily or Atlas/Lily, I'm glad that Lily was able to find peace for her and Emmy.<br><br>As for Atlas, I liked him but I didn't love him. Definitely nowhere near my love for Ryle. I wasn't exactly rooting for Atlas but I wouldn't have minded if Lily chose him in the end. However, I still very much preferred Ryle regardless. I just felt that Atlas was the typical knight in shining armor. Typical good guy you run to. His background story was interesting but him as a character... not so much. He just felt so ordinary and predictable. I wanted to ship Atlas and Lily because let's face it, the signs were practically being shoved down our throats, and although the relationship between Ryle and Lily was developing, Atlas's presence was a like a thorn on your side you just couldn't shake off. But I just couldn't bring myself to ship them blindly like I did with Ryle and Lily.<br><br>Unfortunately, I was too far gone and too far in love with the idea of Ryle and Lily to make room for Atlas and because of that, I'm not sure if I'll ever be fully satisfied with that ending. I was happy that Lily was no longer a victim of domestic abuse. I'm glad that after all that happened between them, Lily and Ryle parted on good terms. I'll forever be heartbroken over the idea of what could've been. And I feel indifferent to Lily and Atlas. Sorry not sorry, Atlas. That basically sums up all my feelings in a nutshell.<br><br>To be honest, I was actually feeling a bit more bitter than I'm making it seem after that ending. But after reading the author's note, it really put things in perspective for me and made me look at the story with brand new eyes. I developed a new understanding and appreciation for the story behind the story.<br><br>I was dying for Ryle and Lily to have their happy ending. Until the very end, I was still rooting for them. It's such an ugly confession to make especially when the couple you're rooting for is toxic and abusive. And I think I feel this way because I never, and hopefully I never will, had to experience abuse. I don't know what it's like and what goes on in the minds of the abused. Colleen did such an excellent job at creating the perfectly imperfect man that was Ryle. Abuse in books has always been a trigger for me and if it were any other book I think I would've put this book down by the first incident of abuse. But Colleen just made you fall so deeply in love with a character that even you couldn't bring yourself to hate him even if you wanted to. YOU were the Lily of this story. But unfortunately, I don't think my Lily would've had the courage to leave. I really wish I could say that I would leave in an instant, but I think I would honestly be lying to myself. You can tell yourself that if you were in Lily's position you would leave in a blink of an eye, but things wouldn't be as easily said and done if you were the one who was actually experiencing it all. And in truth, I think this is exactly what Colleen wanted us to actually sit down and think about because victims who've experienced abuse wouldn't be rooting for Ryle and Lily. I wouldn't be rooting for Ryle and Lily. It just goes to show how much of a struggle it really is to walk away from someone you love and loves you back in all the wrong ways. I usually never read the author's notes after the book but I'm really glad I took the time to read Colleen's story. It really did make me see the situation from a different perspective.<br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I'd been having a bad CoHo streak for three books in a row (if you're curious, the books were — in order — Hopeless, November 9, and Too Late) and for a moment there I was beginning to think that I was doomed to never enjoy another book written by Colleen Hoover again. But PRAISE. It Ends With Us restored my faith completely in the CoHo hype. Not that I was ever planning NOT to read any more of Colleen's books! Colleen Hoover is 100 percent my favorite auto-buy author. I will always buy her books no matter if I end up loving them or not, and with good reason because Colleen is such an exceptional writer. It Ends With Us still wasn't able to top Ugly Love as my favorite CoHo book of all time but I really enjoyed this book more than I thought I would.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="17676772113118455624" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1938388425" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1938388425" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1938388425?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471156267" href="/book/show/29626641-it-ends-with-us">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1938388425" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14628148435672654157"><i>“As hard as this choice is, we break the pattern before the pattern breaks us.”</i><br/><br/>This is my first Colleen Hoover novel. So far I've stayed away from her books for several reasons. You might even call it prejudice, but my judgement didn't fail me. Here's why:<br/>First of all Colleen's ratings are mile high and I'm usually a little doubtful when it comes to that. I just have this feeling that this novel/author is very likely overrated.<br/>Second of all the plot synopsis of every single one of her books seem</span>
  <span id="freeText14628148435672654157" style="display:none"><i>“As hard as this choice is, we break the pattern before the pattern breaks us.”</i><br /><br />This is my first Colleen Hoover novel. So far I've stayed away from her books for several reasons. You might even call it prejudice, but my judgement didn't fail me. Here's why:<br />First of all Colleen's ratings are mile high and I'm usually a little doubtful when it comes to that. I just have this feeling that this novel/author is very likely overrated.<br />Second of all the plot synopsis of every single one of her books seems - how do I say that without sounding mean? - boring. Uncreative. It's always the same in a way. Like Nicholas Sparks (who by the way is a huge homophobe which is the one big reason I'll never ever read one of his books or watch his movies) you know exactly what to expect. A pretty, white and probably starcrossed couple falling in love. Lots of melodrama. A few big shock moments here and there. You know what I'm talking about.<br />The third reason: It's just so straight. And I love a fair share of gay. And I really don't care for straight sex scenes.<br /><br />About this book:<br />Ah well sometimes even I am a slut for clichés and Colleen hits them all. She's a pro. So yes I rolled my eyes a during the first few pages when a tall, dark, hot stranger meets the main character on a rooftop in the middle of the night and they immediately share their deepest thoughts with each other. But secretly I also enjoyed it. I enjoyed their perfect lives and their luxury and the fact that a 24-year-old girl opened a successful and even revolutionary flower shop. I mean, sure why not.<br />The characters seemed fine but the only one I really cared about was Atlas. He really seemed to have character depth while the others just fell a little flat. But then again this is not the kind of novel where I expect the characters to be complex.<br />The names are just horrible. Gosh honestly, this is so typically American, such a white people thing. "Let's just add an 'e' to my brother Rile's name and that's exactly what I'll call my daughter. Rilee." "I love Ellen Degeneres and Finding Nemo so my daughter's middle name will be Dory. And by the way, my name is Lily Blossom Bloom, nice to meet you." Do I have to say more? Yup, my head hurts from rolling my eyes this much.<br /><br />Now this book tackles one big topic and it's called domestic violence and abusive relationships. And in my opinion, Colleen did a good job of portraying them. Of course, I have no experience with this particular matter so I can only judge it from the outside. But as the author explained in her afterword every (abusive) relationship is different and plays out differently. She herself wrote about a young woman's struggle to free herself from this violence. It wasn't an easy fight and she will probably have to fight it in the future. Of course, I wished for her to end it right when it started, but this often isn't the reality. Then again it's a book, which has the power to set an example for other men and women and it shouldn't even have gone this far. But then again it wouldn't have pictured the struggle a person faces when he or she experiences such violence. You see, this discussion could go on and on.<br /><br />In a nutshell: I didn't connect with any of the characters or got emotionally involved in any other way, but it's an entertaining book with a surprisingly deep turn.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/kaispellmeier/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14628148435672654157" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1728424100?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kainat 《HUFFLEPUFF &amp; PROUD》" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kainat 《HUFFLEPUFF &amp; PROUD》" href="/user/show/14717996-kainat-hufflepuff-proud">Kainat 《HUFFLEPUFF &amp; PROUD》</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14717996-kainat-hufflepuff-proud?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1728424100" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8244159162344395925"><i>
  <b>"Everything Shatters. <br/>My tears, my heart, my laughter, my soul. <br/>Shattered like broken glass, raining down around me." </b>
</i><br/><br/>At least now the title makes sense! <br/><br/>Boy, do i have a few thing to say about this It Ends With Us! When i decided to give this a second chance this is not what i had on mind. It wasn't supposed to happen, damn it. <br/><br/>First of all, this Goodreads synopsis is misleading. It needs to be replaced. Whoever came up with it deserves getting fired. <br/><br/>What is the matter with GR users?! Firs</span>
  <span id="freeText8244159162344395925" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>"Everything Shatters. <br>My tears, my heart, my laughter, my soul. <br>Shattered like broken glass, raining down around me." </b>
</i><br><br>At least now the title makes sense! <br><br>Boy, do i have a few thing to say about this It Ends With Us! When i decided to give this a second chance this is not what i had on mind. It wasn't supposed to happen, damn it. <br><br>First of all, this Goodreads synopsis is misleading. It needs to be replaced. Whoever came up with it deserves getting fired. <br><br>What is the matter with GR users?! First, ACoMaF wins "best YA fantasy" award, then this.. THIS!! won Goodreads Choice "Romance"? What's wrong with you people?! Let's get one thing straight, <b>THIS IS NOT A ROMANCE!</b> This "award" was the reason why I've been somewhat skeptical for this long. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471850759ra/20113923.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Why i was so disappointed in Hoover's other book, Ugly Love, is because THIS is what i was expecting from Ugly Love. This has it all. This is what i call love at it's worst. Don't get me wrong, there were love and a dreadful "love story", I still won't call it a romance. I can't thank enough Hoover for not romanticizing abusive behaviors. Thank you, Colleen! <br><br>No, i am not someone who has dealt with anything like this personally, but i am someone who always asks the question "why stay with someone if aren't treating you with the respect you deserve?" I'd like to say i am a bit more aware that it's not always that easy. Still not fully convinced, but a little closer. baby steps, people, baby steps. <br><br>First half was a bit boring &amp; fairly predictable, to be completely honest. It felt like just another typical CH romance. In fact, it wasn't until the last quarter when i started seeing what Hoover was aiming for. Lilly is a very strong character with hidden depths. I am astonished &amp; extremely proud of her. Ryle, on the other hand, is much more complex. No, i don't hate him. If anything, i'm grief-stricken. The ending was perfect. That's what impressed me the most. <br><br>Last but not least, thank you, Mary, for putting up with me. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461211004ra/18838084.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>Thoughts 20% in,</b><br><br>*If some random person literally gets on their knees &amp; begs you to "fuck them" even though you've repeatedly declined such generous offer, that's a giant red flag. There is an extremely high chance they are psychopathic. What you should do is, RUN! RUN FOR YOUR DEAR LIEF. Not swoon.<br><br><br><br>Buddy read with this sweetie pie, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary</a><br><br>I've read 3 Collen Hoover books so far but unfortunately, none of them i found to be very impressive.<br><br>Hopeless. ☆<br>Slammed. ☆ ☆<br>Ugly Love. ☆ ☆<br><br> You know what they say, 4th time's the charm. <br>Keeping my fingers crossed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8244159162344395925" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer7538379112417858023">I don't know what happened with this review. It wasn't whole, the likes gone, and the conversations about the book was gone.   <span id="freeText7538379112417858023" style="display:none">I don't know what happened with this review. It wasn't whole, the likes gone, and the conversations about the book was gone. The audio re-read was great!! <br><br><b>Used my bookmark! ♥</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1476195126i/20811588._SY540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book chewed me up and spit me back out. I said I wasn't going to cry, I cried a little. <br><br><b>NO SPOILERS</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476374106ra/20834433.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book is very deep. It touched on some strong subjects. I would like to add so many excerpts (good and bad) but I'm not going to do that either. I would like for those that haven't read the book yet to go into it without knowing too much. <br><br>There are two people in the book I didn't like, one is from Lily's past (her father) and one is from her current life (Ryle)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476374815ra/20834511.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>I very much loved: <br><br>1) Atlas<br>2) Atlas <br>3) Atlas<br>4) Allysa<br>5) Marshall<br>6) Brad<br>7) Darin<br>8) Jimmy<br>9) Lily's Mom</b><br><br>Obviously, I really loved Atlas because I added his name three times (there are not three of him). <br><br>Allysa is Ryle's sister and Marshall is her husband. Allysa becomes best friends with Lily and helps Lily with the opening of her flower shop and works there with her for some time. <br><br>Brad, Darin and Jimmy are characters that are only in the book for a short period of time, but that short period had me laughing out loud and I really needed that with all of the deep stuff in the book. <br><br>Lily's mom had many issues to deal with but I still loved her because she was a good person. Letting bad things happen to you doesn't make you a bad person. <br><br>The story goes back and forth from when Lily was younger (teens) and when she's a little older. There are a lot of bad things that happened in her childhood. She also meets Atlas when she's a teenager too. They both have troubles they are going through but they had a wonderful bond. <br><br>I'm going to leave it at that because there are so many strong emotions I have over this book, I'm afraid to say anything else. I loved it and I hated it. <b>And it has the most wonderful ending! I'm am so very happy with that ending ♥</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1476374815i/20834512._SY540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>♥ Fin ♥<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/10/it-ends-with-us-by-colleen-hoover.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1730860803?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2016</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1730860803" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15675100746142662335"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>There are so many things I want to say. <br/>So many feelings I'm dying to share.<br/>And way too many thoughts clouding my mind.<br/><br/>This is definitely a book that needs to be discussed thoroughly, but not in a review. Not at the chance of ruining the experience for someone else. This is one that you’ll want to share with your friends, your sister and maybe even your mother. At least, that’s how I felt. Whether or not you ever find yourself in this situation, chances are, you might know someone who i</span>
  <span id="freeText15675100746142662335" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br /><br />There are so many things I want to say. <br />So many feelings I'm dying to share.<br />And way too many thoughts clouding my mind.<br /><br />This is definitely a book that needs to be discussed thoroughly, but not in a review. Not at the chance of ruining the experience for someone else. This is one that you’ll want to share with your friends, your sister and maybe even your mother. At least, that’s how I felt. Whether or not you ever find yourself in this situation, chances are, you might know someone who is. <br /><br /><b>For me, the beauty of this book was the author’s ability to change my perspective.</b> To go from a place of judgment to one of confusion, agony and ultimately understanding. It made me step back and look at a situation that should have been cut and dry or black and white and consider every shade of gray. <br /><br />I’m not going to lie, my headspace was a complete mess and my heart ached. I wanted so desperately for things to be <i>different</i>. For things to be <i>easy</i>. For the right choice to be blatantly obvious. To forgive and forget. To give in to those feelings and accept the bad with the hope that the good would somehow make up for it in the end. <br /><br />This story really hit home with the notion that love is what makes things hard sometimes, not the hurt. Love has the power to blur the lines of acceptance. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>“Naked truths aren’t always pretty.”</b>
</i><br /><br />MY NAKED TRUTH: I told myself awhile ago, I was done with CoHo. That I would never read another of her books, ever. And there was a part of me that almost managed to forget the addictive quality of her writing. <i>Almost</i>. I can honestly say, this was a powerful book. One I’m better for reading. It managed to make me look at things a little differently and I love that. I appreciate that. So thanks, Ms. Hoover.<br /><br /><i>*Complimentary copy provided by Atria and NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.</i></span>

<div id="review_1165944690" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1165944690" />
    <a title="Linda Kage" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3531137-linda-kage"><img alt="Linda Kage" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513777429p2/3531137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1165944690?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda Kage" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda Kage" href="/user/show/3531137-linda-kage">Linda Kage</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3531137-linda-kage?shelf=2016-favorite">2016-favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3531137-linda-kage?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1165944690" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8253429953325830619">Dear Ellen DeGeneres,<br/><br/>I should probably start out with an apology. I don't think I've seen a single one of your talk show episodes all the way through. I catch five or six-minute clips here and there posted every so often on Facebook, and I have loved every single one of them, so I don't know why I haven't watched more. You're totally awesome. <br/><br/>And another confession: I haven't seen Finding Dory yet, either, even though I loved Finding Nemo. So, yeah, I'm sorry about that too.<br/><br/>But I'm so curious ri</span>
  <span id="freeText8253429953325830619" style="display:none">Dear Ellen DeGeneres,<br /><br />I should probably start out with an apology. I don't think I've seen a single one of your talk show episodes all the way through. I catch five or six-minute clips here and there posted every so often on Facebook, and I have loved every single one of them, so I don't know why I haven't watched more. You're totally awesome. <br /><br />And another confession: I haven't seen Finding Dory yet, either, even though I loved Finding Nemo. So, yeah, I'm sorry about that too.<br /><br />But I'm so curious right now if you've read It End With Us by Colleen Hoover, since you know, you're such a big part of the story. The way she incorporated you into everything, with the "just keep swimming" line and watching episodes of your show and the writing letters to you thing to show the backstory, that was really weird but also different and unique (sorry, I know those two words mean the same thing, but I had to use both anyway). I ended up liking your role in the book a lot. <br /><br />But I'm beginning to believe CoHo has a really evil, diabolical brain. She schooled me so bad.<br /><br />I went in thinking...well, I don't even know what I went in thinking. But I know I don't think that way anymore. I think my entire way of thinking has changed. <br /><br />I tried to compartmentalize. Oh, this is going to be a romance story. Well...it was and yet it wasn't. Then I thought it was going to be a love triangle like Maybe Someday was, and yet it totally wasn't. When the heroine Lily started going back and forth in time, telling two stories about a girl falling in love with two different boys in two different portions of her life, I thought it was going to be another version of Ugly Love, except maybe twisted with Lily taking on Miles's role. But it totally wasn't.<br /><br />This was not a light-hearted story. It was not an easy, feel-good, happily-ever-after that you can crawl into to escape from reality story. It didn't even have a real definitive HEA. I can list all kinds of things that it wasn't and didn't have, but I can't pin-point exactly what it WAS and DID have, except maybe a lesson in life. <br /><br />I feel as if I just lived what Lily lived through. I feel as if I can never victim blame again when it comes to an abused spouse. I can never automatically think "why did she stay with him?" because now I know why. All because of Colleen Hoover's diabolical evilness, now I have experienced falling in love with one of those guys and being hurt by him and loved by him, and yet still excusing and forgiving his actions, not just once, not just twice, but every time. <br /><br />Right up into the very last chapter of the book, I was okay with whatever decision Lily made to stay or not to stay with him, because he really wasn't a bad guy. He just did some bad things. And what she did decide was good, but sad, and yet...I don't even know. But I was okay with it. <br /><br />So yeah...I'm really curious how you feel about being mixed up in all this heaviness and serious-issue business. Personally, it's not the kind of story I usually like to read. Stuff that's just too real like that usually gives me hives, and I doubt I want to go out looking for any more stories like this, but I can't say I regret it either. It was just that amazing and just that powerful. <br /><br />Like I said, I was totally schooled by it, and now I go forth with a different outlook on relationships and love and hurting the people who are the closest to you. But I wouldn't want to be schooled this way with every book. I really do need that unrealistic escape more often than not.<br /><br />But I think it was really neat how important you were in the lives of these characters, Ellen, just by being famous and throwing out some witty lines like you do. It really makes you think how everything you say and do can make such an impact on a complete stranger's life, just like Colleen Hoover has now made in mine. <br /><br />And now I feel the need to find some light, fluffy, happy crap to console myself with after reading that life-altering experience. Thanks for listening to me babble!<br /><br />Many hugs and happy reading,<br />Linda Kay <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8253429953325830619" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1733241276" />
    <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters"><img alt="Elyse  Walters" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514246949p2/597461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1733241276?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elyse  Walters" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters">Elyse  Walters</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1733241276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11659682941305632687">Audiobook:<br/><br/>Agree.. agree... agree... with all 3,743 - 5 star ratings!!!!!!! <br/><br/>I didn't think it would happen...but there came a point when tears were welling in my eyes. <br/>I was absolutely exhausted from this mornings hike. I took a little deep sleep afternoon nap - When I opened my eyes, I found Paul resting beside me. <br/>I said..."do you mind.......LISTENING TO THIS AUDIOBOOK"? I was still too sleepy-tired to put my eyes to work reading from my kindle or a physical book. Plus ....I knew I was almost a</span>
  <span id="freeText11659682941305632687" style="display:none">Audiobook:<br /><br />Agree.. agree... agree... with all 3,743 - 5 star ratings!!!!!!! <br /><br />I didn't think it would happen...but there came a point when tears were welling in my eyes. <br />I was absolutely exhausted from this mornings hike. I took a little deep sleep afternoon nap - When I opened my eyes, I found Paul resting beside me. <br />I said..."do you mind.......LISTENING TO THIS AUDIOBOOK"? I was still too sleepy-tired to put my eyes to work reading from my kindle or a physical book. Plus ....I knew I was almost at the very end of this story. <br />Paul said, "sure". He had listened to part of this book on our drive to and from Felton early this morning- to "Fall Creek"... where we hiked 2.5 hours. He was aware - taking in - much of this story too. <br /><br />Right when the issues - messages - of this novel had hit me the hardest-- Paul was lying next to me. HE HEARD WHAT WAS GOING ON. - WE DISCUSSED THE issues - at some point - later - but at that moment, <br />I turned off the audio - not wanting to get to the VERY END...even though - by now - I KNEW WHAT was coming .....and I reached for Paul to snuggle. I had never felt more grateful and thankful. I wanted to cry - didn't - but felt an urge. I WISHED I COULD TELL EVERY WOMAN ON THIS PLANET THAT I FELT CONNECTED TO THEM!!! <br />My quiet moment of being in Paul's arms were comforting.... (my mind was swimming with thoughts - while emotions were circulating through my body). <br /><br />This HIGHLY RATED NOVEL is NOT "The Great Gatsby", "To Kill A Mockingbird", "Anna Karena", "Ulysses", "Jane Austin", "Steven King", "Gone With The Wind", or even "Harry Potter".......<br />SO WHAT IS GOING ON??? <br />Personally-- I think it's so well written -- we aren't aware of the writing at all. The writing seems invisible- WHICH IS IMPOSSIBLE- but TRUE. -- The story is a breathing entity: a living being. <br /><br /> ....what I'm sad about -- is that it took THIS BOOK ( an author I had never read before - pre- judged &amp; pooh-poohed as a chickie-light-weight-mushy-author) ---to KNOCK SOME OLD RIGHTEOUS MARBLES OUT OF MY HEAD!! I NEVER UNDERSTOOD WHY WOMEN WOULD ***EVER*** STAY IN A RELATIONSHIP IF THEIR PARTNER HIT THEM!!!! ( even once). <br />Wow..... I get it: ITS COMPLICATED!!!!!<br /><br />I'm still not sure if I'll read any other books by "Colleen Hoover", or not, but this book deserves all those high ratings. I'm transformed from this journey. <br /><br />Another 5 star rating from me too!!!! A HIGH 5 star rating!!!!!! <br /><br />*note: I honestly don't even consider this a review. It took me 3 minutes to write-- it came straight from my heart---and there's no effort in that!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11659682941305632687" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
