<span id="freeTextContainer5084482072347920852"><b>*****5 STARS*****</b><br/><br/>This is not my real review, please read the unfiltered review here... <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://prettymessreading.wordpress.com/2017/02/10/it-ends-with-us-by-colleen-hoover/'>https://prettymessreading.wordpress.c...</a><br/><br/>So here the thing...<br/>I am struggling writing this review because it hits so close to home. Because of that fact this isn’t going to be written like my normal reviews, it will be about me and Lily. It will be a correlation of our lives.<br/><br/>As I read this book the little broken girl inside me started coming out. I wanted to put her back. I didn’t want her resurface. I needed he</span>
  <span id="freeText5084482072347920852" style="display:none"><b>*****5 STARS*****</b><br><br>This is not my real review, please read the unfiltered review here... <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://prettymessreading.wordpress.com/2017/02/10/it-ends-with-us-by-colleen-hoover/">https://prettymessreading.wordpress.c...</a><br><br>So here the thing...<br>I am struggling writing this review because it hits so close to home. Because of that fact this isn’t going to be written like my normal reviews, it will be about me and Lily. It will be a correlation of our lives.<br><br>As I read this book the little broken girl inside me started coming out. I wanted to put her back. I didn’t want her resurface. I needed her to go back to her hiding place where the adult Danielle wouldn’t find her… She came out nonetheless.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486784008i/21949534._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I spent my childhood from 6 months to 12 years old in a 3 bedroom, 2 1/2 bathroom, 2 car garage house from hell. My mother had a job at a warehouse and my step-father owned his own construction company. We went to church every Sunday where my step-father’s brother was the preacher. We were clean, never hungry and went on family vacations. It looked perfect from the outside. But the inside was a completely different story.<br><br>Unlike Lily, my step-father’s abuse reached my brother, sister, and me. I learned from an early age how to take a few blows from a man. It became so normal that they didn’t even hurt anymore.<br><br><b>But let’s talk about It Ends With Us…</b><br><br>I fell in love with Ryle during the beginning of the book. He was sexy, smart, good in bed – everything I girl could ask for. He was attentive even with his busy schedule at the hospital. He worked for Lily’s heart and never took her love for granted.<br><br>Lily was funny as hell. I loved her from the first paragraph. I thought, “This is a chick I could rock with.” Plus she was a red head. My inner lesbian has a thing for red heads. She was a badass. She was a woman who knew her self-worth and I loved that about her.<br><br>When the two of them came together it was pure magic. Here’s this man who doesn’t want anything that resembles love in his life but couldn’t help himself from falling in love with her. That’s one of my favorite things to read about and to see in real life.<br><br>Atlas, Atlas, Atlas! He was just… perfection! I want an Atlas when I grow up. I really enjoyed reading Lily’s letters to Ellen Degeneres. Getting inside Lily’s head, seeing Atlas the way she did made me love him too. I became so conflicted as to who I wanted Lily to be with.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486784008i/21949535._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>From this day forward, for better, for worse, for richer, for poorer, in sickness and health, until death do us part.”<br><br>Maybe those vows weren’t meant to be taken as literally as some spouses that time.<br><br>For better, for worse?<br><br>Fuck.<br><br>That.<br><br>Shit.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>I’ll be honest, it was hard to hate Ryle. Even after everything he did there was a piece of me who hoped he could change. I think that that scared little girl in me wanted to believe he would stop, like I prayed my step-father would.<br><br>This is one of those books everyone has to read for themselves to find their voice on it. It's not a book to be reviewed, it's a book to be felt.<br><br>Follow all my crazy...<br>Blog <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://prettymessreading.wordpress.com/">https://prettymessreading.wordpress.com/</a><br>Instagram <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.instagram.com/prettymessreading/">https://www.instagram.com/prettymessr...</a><br>Facebook <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/prettymessreading/">https://www.facebook.com/prettymessre...</a><br>Twitter <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twitter.com/prettymessread">https://twitter.com/prettymessread</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5084482072347920852" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1692154210" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1692154210" />
    <a title="Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8524618-angie---angie-s-dreamy-reads"><img alt="Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578074503p2/8524618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1692154210?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads" href="/user/show/8524618-angie---angie-s-dreamy-reads">Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1692154210" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18317360166543258460"><b>SPEECHLESS. </b><br/><br/>This book left me completely speechless. It's why this review will be far from eloquent and admittedly a little short. I've been staring at the cursor as it blinks in silence on my computer screen, trying to come up with a review for this unbelievably complex, astonishingly real, and heart wrenching novel. I can't decide what I want to tell you and I think that's because I really <b>
  <u>don't want to tell anything at all.</u>
</b><br/><br/>I went into <i>It Ends with Us</i> with a clear head and absolutely no id</span>
  <span id="freeText18317360166543258460" style="display:none"><b>SPEECHLESS. </b><br /><br />This book left me completely speechless. It's why this review will be far from eloquent and admittedly a little short. I've been staring at the cursor as it blinks in silence on my computer screen, trying to come up with a review for this unbelievably complex, astonishingly real, and heart wrenching novel. I can't decide what I want to tell you and I think that's because I really <b>
  <u>don't want to tell anything at all.</u>
</b><br /><br />I went into <i>It Ends with Us</i> with a clear head and absolutely no idea on what was going to happen. It's best that way. This novel is one of those reads that simply knocks you out cold. It's a heavy handed, physical blast to the feels <i>(aka: emotions).</i> You <i>cannot</i> catch your breath while reading. It's settles you into an easy reading pace, makes you feel good, cocoons you in it's warmth, and then when you think you're happy and safe, you're not. <br /><br />It <b>EVISCERATES</b> you. <br /><br />It tears you down piece by piece until you're left confused, torn, broken, thinking, <i>"I can't believe this is happening. I don't believe it. I don't want to believe it." </i><br /><br />I still can't get over it. I still can't process the fact that it threw me so off center. And when I describe this book to people, I keep repeating, <b>"It's heart breaking, but hopeful."</b> And I know that doesn't seem really comforting. It doesn't tell you much at all. <br /><br />But here's the thing, I don't want to get into Ryle or Atlas or Lily or the characters in this book. I don't want to break them down piece by piece. I don't want to plant seeds or ideas in your head. I don't want to influence your reading experience. I want you to go in. I want you to <b>READ.</b> I want you to <b>EXPERIENCE</b> it with the same innocence and naivety that I did. <br /><br />I want it to <b>sucker</b> punch you. <br />I want it to <b>ruin</b> you. <br />I want it to <b>heal</b> you. <br /><br />I want you to <b>
  <i>LIVE</i>
</b> this through Lily's eyes, heart, and mind just like I did. And I feel as though saying anything to you, about anything, is a spoiler. And that is why this review is so pathetic. It's why this review is a short, hot mess. <br /><br /><i>ARC received in exchange for an honest review </i><br /><br /><b><u>FOLLOW ME ON:</u> <a href="https://www.facebook.com/AngiesDreamyReads" rel="nofollow noopener">FACEBOOK</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/angiesdreamyreads/" rel="nofollow noopener">INSTAGRAM</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Angie_McKeon" rel="nofollow noopener">TWITTER</a> | <a href="http://www.angieandjessicasdreamyreads.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">BLOG</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="18317360166543258460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deanna " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deanna " href="/user/show/15662887-deanna">Deanna </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781508212690" href="/book/show/27408565-it-ends-with-us">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1748671872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16770000538819036277">My reviews can also be seen at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpress.com'>https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpr...</a><br/><br/>Wow!<br/><br/>I am a bit late to the party for this one. I'm not sure what I can say that hasn't been said already. <br/><br/>This was my first CoHo book and it looks like I picked a good one to start with. It's surprising but even though the book had already been out for a while, other than hearing that it was very emotional, I didn't actually know what it was about. I am happy I was able to listen to it without knowing very much. It didn't ta</span>
  <span id="freeText16770000538819036277" style="display:none">My reviews can also be seen at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpress.com">https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpr...</a><br /><br />Wow!<br /><br />I am a bit late to the party for this one. I'm not sure what I can say that hasn't been said already. <br /><br />This was my first CoHo book and it looks like I picked a good one to start with. It's surprising but even though the book had already been out for a while, other than hearing that it was very emotional, I didn't actually know what it was about. I am happy I was able to listen to it without knowing very much. It didn't take very long to see where the story-line was headed. The book's main theme deals with a very delicate and important subject.<br /><br />I can understand the variety of feelings this book brings out in different people. I've seen reviews from friends that absolutely love this book and some from friends that really didn't care for it. I can see both sides. I fall in the middle but more towards really liking it. Does that make sense? I don't know... but that's the best way I think I can describe how I feel about it.<br /><br />I've now listened to handful of audio-books and I'm really enjoying them. I will always love to read books but on those days where I have a headache or my eyes are bothering me, it's awesome to have this choice. In my opinion the narrator for this novel did a wonderful job.....Olivia Song (Great name too!).<br /><br />"It Ends With Us" is a heartbreaking novel that deals with sensitive and extremely important issues and I think that Colleen Hoover handled it well. <br /><br />Sometimes you have to tell yourself...<br /><br />“Just keep swimming.” </span>

<div id="review_1167326844" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1167326844" />
    <a title="Jennifer Kyle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9916227-jennifer-kyle"><img alt="Jennifer Kyle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514915429p2/9916227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1167326844?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Kyle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Kyle" href="/user/show/9916227-jennifer-kyle">Jennifer Kyle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9916227-jennifer-kyle?shelf=cry-baby-books">cry-baby-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1167326844" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3132878097600030151"><b>4.5 STARS</b><br/><br/><span>[image error]</span><br/><br/>Colleen Hoover delivers a story that is not only thought provoking but will indeed get those emotions running amuck. Lily Bloom’s story is told well with wit, heart, and a fantastic cast of characters. Fans of this author will not be disappointed in the presentation and heart that she has placed in this book.<br/><br/><b>
  <i> ‘Imagine all the people you meet in your life. There are so many. They come in like waves, trickling in and out with the tide. Some waves are much bigger and make m</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText3132878097600030151" style="display:none"><b>4.5 STARS</b><br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>Colleen Hoover delivers a story that is not only thought provoking but will indeed get those emotions running amuck. Lily Bloom’s story is told well with wit, heart, and a fantastic cast of characters. Fans of this author will not be disappointed in the presentation and heart that she has placed in this book.<br><br><b>
  <i> ‘Imagine all the people you meet in your life. There are so many. They come in like waves, trickling in and out with the tide. Some waves are much bigger and make more of an impact than others. Sometimes the waves bring with them things from deep in the bottom of the sea and they leave those things tossed onto the shore. Imprints against the grains of sand that prove the waves had once been there, long after the tide recedes.’</i>
</b><br><br>In chatting with friends and reading other’s opinions on the outcome of the story I’m left with so many, hell too many conflicting feelings. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I do think Ryle was redeemable if the author so wanted however I got the pain of what became of their love and survivors need never to go back. (If anyone has a shot of fighting his abusive infliction it would be an extremely intelligent and educated man who has a solid family to support him and a strong will and reasons to do so.) From reading the author's note for the third time last night she wanted to pattern him around her father but her father was an alcoholic who if I read it right didn't help her mother financially when she left or the kids. I think perhaps she didn't go hard enough with Ryle's character because I do think a therapist would find all his qualities, smart, driven, no drug or alcohol problem in the mix, strong support system and will to change a perfect patient to overcome his rage. Also, Atlas was so darn convenient just there on the outer rim of this story waiting to bounce back into Lily’s world. Don’t get me wrong, I liked him a lot but the love connection for me was with Ryle not her childhood friend. Though the ending between Ryle and Lily worked for me it was heartbreaking yet real and I cried and cried for them. To my shock it seems that I read this one a certain way and double the number of friends read it as Atlas and Lily’s love story from the get go. Crazy Right but the easiest way to see where you fall is how you answer this question - Was this a hea?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> So you can see my confusion yet the author’s skill in leaving both impressions to be received by readers. <br><br><b>
  <i>"It's not a person's actions that hurt the most. It's the love. If there was no love attached to the action, the pain would be a little easier to bear."</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491944107ra/22465381.gif" width="430" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="3132878097600030151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jfTEdy/C9c+szAemv20uiLYQ18TVWuK24wGPxWMCpEquaiaspZyNoHC9B2wXcPXw9uDPmAid2bXnqepDb+pRXA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xu+YMgkiY8FGldJR1eyYD8k/XmddFRtXHeXkPlV0ueblcXrpg3wbrprk0pt98UN3ic9GO4DSIFQZTYG4WZxM8A==')})
  }

You were rocking back on your heels, balancing on that thick yellow line that runs along the subway platform, waiting for the F train. I didn’t know it was you until it was too late, and then you were gone. Again. You said my name; I saw it on your lips. I tried to will the train to stop, just so I could say hello.\n\nAfter seeing you, all of the youthful feelings and memories came flooding back to me, and now I’ve spent the better part of a month wondering what your life is like.
